Justification:

Examples of Quality Control/Testing purchases include:

Cooling Turbine Starter Test Cell
The purpose of this procurement is to upgrade the Cooling Turbine Test Cell located in Building 137. This project will include all new data acquisition and
control system, air valves, pressure transducers, wiring and upgraded units under test (UUTs) test carts. The current test cell has far exceeded its useful life and
several components are obsolete.

Automated FPI Line
The purpose of this project is to replace the Automated Penetrant Inspection System currently located in Building 4225. This penetrant line is used to inspect
cracks, pits, corrosion and defects in the aircraft subassemblies.

Hand Clean Stripping Tanks (5), B137
The purpose for this project is to replace the existing Hand Stripping Tanks. The current tanks have exceeded their expected service life and pose functional
and safety risks. A complete system replacement is necessary to ensure operational continuity.

Valve Channel 3 Test Stand
The purpose of this procurement is to replace the Valve Channel 3 Test Stand in building 137. A new and modernized valve adapter system will significantly
reduce setup and installation times for systems under test as well as produce more accurate flow data by reducing air leakage.


                                                                                                                                Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
 Meandering Winder Magnetometer
The purpose of this project is to procure new Meandering Winding Magnetometers to be installed in Building 4026. The existing equipment is significantly
limited in capability, incurs a significant amount of downtime, and only supports the H53 platform. The new equipment will expand existing capacity to cover
the HK53, F35 and M135 platforms. The new Meandering Winding Magnetometers are expected to operate on average 1000 hours per year with significantly
less maintenance required than the current system.

Scanning Electron Microscope
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing Scanning Electron Microscope facing increased downtime and parts obsolescence. The Scanning Electron
Microscope is critical to assess the failure modes of aircraft subassemblies and routinely used to ensure the safety of flight for aircraft. If not upgraded, the
reduced capacity will lead to increased backlog of inspections.

Examples of Machinery purchases include:

CNC Milling Machine, B83
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing CNC Mill that currently supports all aircraft platforms at FRCE. The current CNC Mill is nearing its life
limit in terms of holding tolerances and maintainability. The CNC Mill is a critical asset to the FRCE mission and will cause significant delays on multiple
platforms if the system is not in continuous operation.

Press Break, B137
This project is to procure a replacement of the existing Wysong Press Brake. The replacement Press Break will provide improved reliability and functionality
required for the workload within the shop. The existing asset presents constant quality issues when conducting intricate bends. Lack of quality in parts due to
poor performance of the existing machine result in a significant volume of rework.

Press Break, B83
This project is to procure a replacement of the existing Wysong Press Brake for Shop 33310/93551. The replacement Press Break will provide improved
reliability and functionality required for the workload within the shop. The existing asset presents constant quality issues when conducting intricate bends. Lack
of quality in parts due to poor performance of the existing machine result in a significant volume of rework.

Vertical Turning Lathe X2
This project will replace one Vertical Tuning Lathes Shop 93567. The existing lathes are starting to fatigue resulting in an increase of down time and
maintenance manhours. The current machine is nearing its useful life and needs to be replaced to prevent workload inefficiencies and unforeseen downtime.
Replacement parts have also been a challenge to obtain.

Gantry 5-Axis Milling Machine, B137
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing 5-Axis milling machine in Building 137. The current system is aging, resulting in and increase of required
maintenance and unplanned down time. Multiple shops throughout FRCE require the use of the 5 axis milling machine and are constantly impacted by the
system’s downtime.

Laser Punch Press (Replace laser Strippet Machine with Trumpt)

                                                                                                                           Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
The purpose of this project is to replace the Laser Strippet Machine with a new Laser/Punch Machine in Building 137. The current system has reached it’s
useful life and is facing significant obsolescence issues. This machine currently supports all aircraft platforms at FRCE

Water jet (Replace Omac Water Jet)
The purpose of this project is to replace the Water Jet Machine in Building 137 which has reached its useful life. The system is starting to have an increased
failure rate and the necessary repairs are taking longer due to the extent of the repairs needed.
Auto Quench Backup (Procure)#14
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing Auto Quench system in Building 137. The current system is unreliable and poses a major safety risk to the
furnace operations creating a significant backlog of orders.

EDM Wire Machine
The purpose of this project is to replace the EDM Wire Machine in Building 4225. This machine currently supports all aircraft platforms here at FRCE. The
current system is reaching the end of its useful life and is starting to have major component failures. Additionally, many of the seals on the doors and pumps are
starting to fail causing major leaks on the machine. Replacement parts are harder to come by which in turn is causing longer down times. If this machine is not
replaced, production will lose capability to work on larger parts at FRCE.

B101 Motch Vertical Grinder Rebuild
The purpose of this project is to procure one new vertical grinder to maintain CNC vertical grinding capabilities at FRCSE. The rebuild of this system is
necessary to minimize the downtime currently experienced. The rebuild is projected to reduce the set-up time by 30%.

CNC Lathes for VRT (2-Ea) - Bldg. 65
The purpose of this project is to procure new, modern, programmable CNC Lathes supporting the Voyage Repair Team (VRT) that performs scheduled
maintenance and emergency services to various aircraft carrier launch/recovery systems. The existing lathes used to manufacture and repair systems parts do
not meet current demands and is limited in capability. Without replacement of the existing lathes, the VRT program will lose the ability to service aircraft
carriers and U.S. Coast Guard shops in a timely fashion.

IVD Retrofit - Bldg. 472
The purpose of this project is to upgrade and retrofit the existing IVD system in Bldg 472 in support of F/A-18 (C,D,E,F,G), E2/C2, H-53, and all other aircraft
requiring aluminum coating in any of their parts. This system is currently inoperable causing workload to be contracted-out to local vendors and increasing the
production costs for these parts. This results in an increase of turnaround time and cost for processing parts. The overhaul of this machine will reduce
errors/process time and reset communications between the control software and the machine itself for more efficient production.

Semi-Automatic Horizontal Boring Jig for VRT
The purpose of this project is to procure a new CNC Horizontal Boring & Milling Machine to replace the antiquated Semi-Automatic Horizontal Boring Mill
used by Voyage Repair Team (VRT). The existing system can no longer reliably find/make threaded holes and requires extensive monthly maintenance due to
irreparable leaks. There are no other boring machines within the VRT program, causing a complete work stoppage with no work-around solutions.

Vertical Turret Grinder (VTG), LM2500

                                                                                                                          Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
The purpose of this project is to procurement of a new Vertical Turret Lathe (VTL) and tooling, in order to bring manufacturing capabilities for LM2500
components back in-house. The new system will increase delivery timelines by 25% while significantly reducing the overall cost to produce the parts.

Examples of Support Equipment purchases include:

Modify/Upgrade X-Ray Equipment
The purpose of this procurement is to Modify/Upgrade X-Ray equipment and vault to accommodate future incoming H-53K rotor blade workload. The engine
air particle separator {EAPS} manipulator will be moved from the vault to outside of the vault. A new vault will be required with the EAPS manipulator. The
FRC needs to upgrade the equipment and move the EAPS manipulator to accommodate the equipment to avoid a single point of failure. The EAPS needs to be
in its own vault so both vaults can operate independently.

Vapor Degreaser
The purpose of this project is to remove a non-functioning Vapor Degreaser and replace it with a new vapor degreaser. The current vapor degreaser will be over
18 years old when replaced. The FRC has established capability of degreasing a plethora of components, which is crucial in processing components for many
platforms. Projected workload will only increase the demand for the degreaser. The procurement will improve hazardous waste control reducing risk to the
artisans and environment.

ASKARS Stackers B137
The purpose of this project is to replace the Automated Storage Kitting and Retrieval System (ASKARS) Large Item Stacker (LIS) and Special Large Item
Stacker (SLIS), with associated control software and hardware. The cranes include optical data communication allowing for a wireless connection to the cranes.
These two material handling systems consists of a trolley and crane to robotically store or retrieve large components among stacks of shelving delivering them
to or from a conveyed staging platform. Supported workload: All aircraft platforms. These stackers are the only remaining devices not replaced from the
original installation of ASKARS equipment around 1980. They have not been mechanically upgraded. Downtime is a problem due to part failure. The usage
and reliance on ASKARS for storing, organizing, kitting and scheduling parts has increased with the depot initiatives to improve production delivery schedules.

Liquid Penetrant Inspection System
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing Rotor Head Liquid Penetrant Inspection System. The Liquid Penetrant line is the primary inspection
station for various Flight Safety Components and is therefore critical to the overall safety of the aircraft. It also serves as a backup station for flight critical
engine and rotating components requiring ultra-high sensitivity. The current workload for the penetrant system is 17,262 hr. /yr. and the future workload is
18,898 hours. There will be improvements in reliability due to fewer deficiencies. A change from a manual system to a semi-automated system will improve
efficiency and consistency. Process time will decrease with a new machine since deficiencies will be eliminated.

AEP Allison Electrophoretic Coating System
The purpose of this project is to upgrade and replace critical high failure components within the Allison Electrophoretic (AEP) Coating System. The upgrades
is projected to significantly reduce the maintenance manhours to repair the current system and increases throughput capacity by 25%.

Jig Bore Rotary Tables (4 for New Mitsui Seiki Jig Bore)

                                                                                                                             Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
This project is to procure new Rotary Tables for the new Jig Bore cell going into building 133. The rotary tables are critical to the proper repair of jig bores.
Without these tables the shop would be severely limited in capacity for the capability needed.

B101 Bearing Cleaning Line Tanks (9)
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing bearing cleaning line with new equipment. HAZMAT spillage and leaks are occurring more frequently
causing downtime. New equipment is project to significantly minimize downtime and maintenance cost.

Computer Tomography (CT) Cabinet
The purpose of this project is Acquire a CT Cabinet system to support FRCSE Material lab. This system is projected to increase the teams’ capability in
reverse engineering of complex geometries and supporting new techniques for FRCSE's NDI X-ray process. CT testing has capabilities that are required for
future technology processing such as cold spray and additive manufacturing. Roughly 11 engineering investigations (EI) are submitted to the lab for failure
analysis that CT can provide support to. The current turnaround time to completing these EIs is 36.6 days. CT can improve the analysis accuracy and reduce the
turnaround time an estimated 10%.

Paint Booth Bldg. 2085 (Mayport)
This effort is to replace the antiquated paint booth located at Mayport Bldg. 2085. The existing booth does not have the structural integrity or space to have an
integral fall-arrest system necessary to perform the required workload. The new booth will be taller to allow in integral fall-arrest system, provide more space
for the artisans, and allows for the use of mobile stands. The new paint booth also utilizes generated heat in the booth for humidity control mitigation purposes
without requiring the entire facility to be heated.

H101S Upgrade Abrasive Blast Booth
This project will upgrade and electrical controls of the existing aircraft abrasive blast booth that supports F/A-18 A-F and H-60 platforms. The current blast
booth and its support equipment is exceeding its expected life and requires a significant number of maintenance man hours to meet the current operational
demands. An upgraded system will add longevity and reduce maintenance downtime.

B795TF34 Main Fuel Control Test Stand Upgrade
The purpose of this project is to upgrade existing TF34 Main fuel control test stand. FRCSE engine fuel accessories maintain the only DOD dedicated test stand
in the inventory. The upgrade is necessary to maintain its capability to meet the evolving fleet demands.

B101 Surface Finish Shop DESIGN
This effort is to design upgrades to the current surface finish shop that incorporates new tanks, supporting structures, ventilation, and support equipment. The
current surface finish shop is in a state of decay, and the equipment is outdated requiring constant maintenance. Several of the tanks lack the proper ventilation
for safety and multiple trip hazards exist due to the older support structure and grating layout.

101W Paint Booth
The purpose of this project is to replace paint booth in 101W to allow for the use of the robotic spraying system. This robotic spray system will be used to apply
organic coatings to flight control surfaces and other miscellaneous flat components. The current paint booth is not configured to allow for the robotic spray
system to be used.



                                                                                                                             Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
B794 Paint Preparation Enclosure & Equipment
The purpose of this project tis to install a climate-controlled (temperature and humidity) paint mixing and storage enclosure for the component paint shop to
meet safety and HAZMAT regulations.


B101 Paint Preparation Enclosure & Equipment
The purpose of this project tis to install a climate-controlled (temperature and humidity) paint mixing and storage enclosure for component paint to meet safety
and HAZMAT regulations.

B794 Fan Case Curing Ovens (2)
This project is intended to replace the two ovens in B794 Engine Finish Shop. The existing ovens have been in operation for more than 38 years exceeding their
useful lifespan.

B101 Surface Finish Shop Equipment
The purpose of this project is to upgrade the critical equipment used in the surface finish shop. The current surface finish shop is in a state of decay and the
equipment is outdated requiring constant maintenance. Several of the tanks lack the proper ventilation for safety and multiple trip hazards exist. The upgrade is
targeted to remedy the safety issues as well as provide modern finish equipment to meet the increased demand on the shop.
Horizontal Balancing Machines (4-Ea)
The purpose of this project is to replace the horizontal balance machines for the LM-2500 program. It is essential for proper engine function that LM-2500
components are accurately balanced prior to engine build-up processes. These machines provide precision balancing of the High Pressure Turbine (HPT) &
Low Pressure Turbine (LPT), Stators, forward & rear shafts, 1st & 2nd-stage disks, Number 3-9 Spools, and Number 11-13 Spools. The current machines are
over 35 years old, almost twice the expected useful service life. They are experiencing increasing incidences of mechanical failure, requiring more corrective
maintenance. New balancing machines will minimize downtime, reduce Corrective Maintenance costs, by nearly 90%, and increase production output of the
LM-2500 program throughout their process.

Vertical Balancing Machines (2-Ea) - Bldg. 472
The purpose of this project is to replace two (2) Vertical Balance Machines for the LM-2500 Program. It is essential for proper engine function that LM-2500
components are accurately balanced prior to engine build-up processes. These machines provide precision balancing of the High Pressure Turbine (HPT) &
Low Pressure Turbine (LPT), Stators, forward & rear shafts, 1st & 2nd-stage disks, Number 3-9 Spools, and Number 11-13 Spools. The current machines are
over 20 years old, and are at their end-of-lifecycle. They are experiencing increasing incidences of mechanical failure, requiring more corrective maintenance.
New balancing machines will minimize downtime, reduce Corrective Maintenance costs, by nearly 90%, and increase production output of the LM-2500
program throughout their process.

Hydraulic Actuator and Flow Test Stand - Bldg. 472
The purpose of this project is to procure a replacement for the existing Hydraulic Actuator Test Stand used to test landing-gear parts. The current system is the
only machine that can assess these parts for functionality, causing a complete work stoppage when it breaks. Additionally, replacement parts are increasingly
difficult to find due to the machine’s age. A new bench is expected to increase program productivity and worker safety.



                                                                                                                          Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
P-1 Plating Line Bldg. 472
The purpose of this project is to modernize the Plating Shop in Building 472. This project will reduce the possibility of hazardous spills, a safety &
environmental concern, and improve processing line efficiency of the P-1 Line. This line directly supports the alkaline de-rusting and cadmium strip processes
for F/A-18 (C/D/E/F/G), H-53, and Voyage Repair Team (VRT) programs. Existing tanks are between 29-48 years old and well beyond current industry life
expectancy of 15 years. Tank-age alone accounts for a high risk of failure that will result in complete work stoppage but also grave safety/environmental
concerns due to the hazardous chemical compounds held within the tanks. Realignment of chemical processing baths in this line will increase production by
removing current inefficiencies and elimination of unnecessary tanks within the line creating a safer and faster process for affected parts. Failure to replace the
tanks & ancillary equipment will continue to work with outdated equipment and risk potential exposure to hazardous solutions such as chrome, nickel, or
chromic acid or risk complete work stoppage with any mishap or safety/environmental event.

P-5 Cadmium Plating Line Bldg. 472
The purpose of this project is to rebuild the cadmium plating line with new components and an efficient shop layout. This line directly supports the application
of Cadmium coating processes for F/A-18 (C/D/E/F/G), H-53, and Voyage Repair Team (VRT) programs. The existing system is at least 30+ years old
whereas current industrial life expectancy for this type of equipment is 15 years. The age of the tanks has already caused leaks, resulting in complete work
stoppage with no other work-around solutions except to outsource the workload to local vendors. Realignment of chemical processing baths in this line will
increase production by removing current inefficiencies and elimination of unnecessary tanks within the line creating a safer and faster process for affected
parts.

P-7 Chrome Line
The purpose of this project is to procure a chrome plating system to replace the outdated chrome plating line supporting the F/A-18, F-35, E-2/D, and V-22
platforms. The system is well beyond its life expectancy of 15 years; many subassemblies are as old as 48 years. Recent leaks from holes in both the liners and
tanks have been found, and one of the tanks is completely inoperable and being replaced. As a result, productivity has been significantly affected. These leaks
are not only a safety, but also an environmental hazard due to the toxic nature of chrome.


Cooling Tower System
This project is to procure a cooling tower system to support the Autoclaves in B250. This system is necessary to assist the autoclaves to maintain specific
temperatures during operation.

PA System for B472, B250, B379, B460, B378, B463
The purpose of this project is to replace Nine PA systems for B463, B379, B250, B472, B94, B470, B785, B378, and B460 at FRCSW. The existing PA
System is currently inoperable in 8 out of 9 buildings. In the event of an emergency, there is no capability to publicly address all FRCSW personnel
simultaneously. This poses a major safety concern as it delays response times to quickly address emergencies (health, security, environmental, natural disasters,
etc.).

Cleaning Shop Ventilation System, B-472
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing ventilation ductwork and fans in the cleaning shop at FRCSW. Current ventilation is inadequate/outdated
and failing which poses a significant safety risk.

                                                                                                                           Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
Lube & Scavenge Jet Engine Test Stand (UF-15), B-379
The purpose of this project is to replace the existing Jet Engine test stand located in the Hydraulic Shop in Building 379. The present test stand is over 51 years
old and parts are extremely hard to find. The shop is in dire need of a new UF-15 test stand, as the existing is obsolete and a single point of failure that
jeopardizes the readiness of the fleet.

Wind Tunnel, B-378
The purpose of this project is to upgrade the Wind Tunnel Test System to support the new AOA of the F/A-18 program. The wind tunnel test system is used to
assess flight characteristics of the new wind-foil designs created by the F/A 18 program. The wind tunnel requires enhancements to allow for the new designs
to be fully tested prior to manufacture.

Conformal Anode Storage System, Plating – B472
The purpose of this effort is to procure a conformal anode storage system and 10 conformal anode fixtures for the plating shop. Currently, the storage area is
inadequate for the existing and new conformal anodes being used by the fleet. Most are currently squeezed into a small storage room, which makes access to
the anodes difficult. This results in an inefficient way to store and inventory the anodes.

Paint Booth, 30FT – B472
This project will replace the existing classified paint booth with a fully enclosed paint booth in Building 472 supporting the F-18 E/F platforms. The existing
booth does not have built-in climate control system resulting in routine delays due to unacceptable humidity and temperature levels.

Paint Booth, 90FT - B472
This project will replace the existing 90FT paint booth with a fully enclosed paint booth in Building 472. The large paint booth is used to paint V-22, F/A-18
A/G, E-2/C-2, H-60, H-1, and H-53 aircraft components. There are currently no climate controls and work is often stopped due to temperature and humidity
fluctuations that are outside of the allowable tolerances. As workload has progressed and components and stands have become larger; the existing paint booth is
not large enough to process these components.


Salt Bath & Heat-Treat Furnace 10 - B472
This project replaces the existing salt bath and heat treat furnaces with state-of-the-art capability supporting the F/A- 18, V-22, E-2C, E-2D, and H-60. The
existing salt bath, heat treat furnace system has far exceeded its expected life. Without the replacement of this system, a possible work stoppage will occur or
the need to outsource components as there is no liquid bath alternative.

Walk-In Blast Booth, VRT
This effort removes the 22 year old blast booth and replaces it with a new turn-key blast booth. This project is projected to significantly minimize inspection
and down time and reduce personnel safety risks, leading to increased throughput.

B1615 PEMB Mezzanine (Mayport)
This project provides a load-bearing Mezzanine to VRT Mayport Bldg. 1615. The Mezzanine is required for short & long-term staging of parts, material, and
components utilized throughout several phases of depot-level overhaul, manufacture, and repair of NAVAIR ALRE, NAVSUP WSS, and SURFLANT

                                                                                                                            Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
Aviation Support Systems. Without the Mezzanine, these materials & components occupy floor space in designated machining and dirty-work areas,
consequently creating work-flow obstructions and work-process delays.

Examples of Computer Hardware (Production):

Network Switch Upgrade

This effort upgrades the obsolescencing network switches that serves as the primary data backbone for the site. The current switched have reached their end of
life expectancy, driving an increase to the annual cost of sustainment. The upgraded network switches are projected to dramatically increase the data
throughput capacity that has routinely plagued site. The increase of capacity will drive enhanced information sharing and collaboration at the respective
business units

Examples of Computer Hardware (Network):

RDT&E Network Switch Upgrade
The intent is to upgrade all RDT&E network switches. The network infrastructure devices are coming to End of Life (EOL) and can only be supported by third
party maintenance. The network infrastructure allows for data traffic throughout the FRCE campus. All services rendered to FRCE, including FST are directly
dependent on this infrastructure.

RDT&E Network Stack Refresh
This effort is to modernize the equipment that comprises the RDT&E Security Stack: Intrusion Prevention System (IPS), perimeter firewall, forwarding proxy,
Domain Name Server (DNS), perimeter router, scanning VLAN router, Virtual Machine (VM) hosting hardware and L2/L3 switches. All RDT&E services
rendered to the Industrial and Engineering labs are directly dependent on these devices.
                                                                                                                               Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
Examples of Telecommunications:

VOIP CISCO Telephone System Replacement
Voice over Internet Protocol, or VoIP, is a type of communication technology (comprising both hardware and software) that allows you to make phone calls
using an internet connection rather than a traditional analog phone line that uses wires or optical fibers to make a connection. The current system is without a
maintenance plan due to a lapse during COVID-19 and a funding shortfall. The voicemail system is not operational at this time. Inevitably the system will fail
without upgrade.

Avaya Telephone Systems Upgrade

The purpose of this project is to replace the obsolete telecommunications and voicemail system site wide. The current system has exceeded is life expectancy
and experiencing an increased failure rate hampering efficient daily communication as well as driving a dramatic increase in maintenance costs. The current
system has also reached its expansion capacity, limiting the sites ability to meet expected demand with new facilities coming on-line.

Justification:

Examples of New Construction purchases include:

Renovation for B143 (RM)
This effort provides for the complete renovation of Bldg. 4172 to house various machine shop component rework machines. These current facility does not
contain the square footage necessary to meet the current machining demands. Additionally higher ceilings and a crane capability is required to work on larger
assemblies that are projected to become a part of the current workload.

Design - New Components Building (VTL) (NF)
This project will replace the existing B4172 and construct a new facility to house larger machine tools supporting the H-53K platform. The existing facilities at
FRCE are not adequate to for a new footprint requirements for the new machinery.


Design - Minor Construction for B4032 (NF)
This project is to renovate Building 4032 to accommodate the laboratory equipment requirements. The renovation will also improve safety of personnel and
protection of materials to prevent contamination.

Modernization for B86 (RM)
This project is to construct facility for the new Vacuum Test Chamber System (VTCS). The existing Vacuum Test Chamber System at FRCE tests various
aircraft pressure regulators and valves supporting several platforms including F/A-18, AV-8B, C-2, P-3, and E-2C. B86 Modernization will include minor
facility construction and new footprint foundation to accommodate the installation of the new test system while allowing the existing test system to remain fully
operational in support of the fleet. This will eliminate high risk concerns and provide flexibility to production as well as the contractor.



                                                                                                                               Exhibit Fund‐9B Capital Investment Justification
 Paint Booth (Fire Riser Room), Bldg. 245 (NF)
This project renovates Bldg. 245 to a new paint booth. Due to age and exposure to paint overspray, the facility infrastructure is severely degraded. The
renovation will include upgrades to aging facilities systems, new foot print (paint/mix, fire protection room, lift storage/charging, & hygiene at 3766), and a
new paint booth.

Lab Addition B4032 (NF)
The purpose of this project is a comprehensive renovation of the lab areas of Building 4032 to create a modern and flexible laboratory environment. The project
will replace laboratory systems which have reached the end of their useful life, create a safe environment for the personnel and provide an environment that
improves the quality and reliability of the research and testing being conducted.

Lean-To, Bldg. 1272 (New Footprint)
The purpose of this project is to remove an existing old metal shelter and replace with a new, larger, semi-enclosed metal-skinned protective structure to
establish the Aviation Support Equipment (ASE) program at FRCSW. This project will expand the new ASE’s program footprint from 1,659-SF to 3,019-SF
to conduct all current maintenance & repair activities performed. Under current circumstances, the ASE team must conduct their work at customers’ locations
on base or move the equipment to a remote location with limited capabilities for efficiency. This expansion will create a dedicated workshop, in a centralized
location, to allow storage of replacement parts for equipment rotating through the shop for routine/scheduled Preventative Maintenance or
Emergency/Corrective Maintenance activities, protect the command’s assets from corrosive, salty-air environments or inclement weather, and improve
efficiencies of the services offered by the ASE group.

Lean-To, Bldg. 336 (New Footprint)
The purpose of this project is to construct a protective semi-enclosed shelter for temporary storage of HAZWASTE materials prior to appropriate off-base
disposal within the established HAZMAT yard of Bldg. 336. The existing 3,575-SF structure is woefully inadequate, frequently leaving barrels of
HAZWASTE (expended oils, cutting fluids, lubricants, etc) exposed to the open-air, corrosive salt environment. Minimizing exposure to alternating salty air
and high daytime full-sun weather conditions creates an undue risk for container failure, leaks, and spills of the hazardous materials stored onsite. A massive
HAZWASTE incident onsite would likely trigger costly cleanup fees as well as governmental fines for noncompliance of current environmental regulations at
both state and national levels.

F-35 AV Storage Building
The purpose of this project is to construct an estimated 12,000-15,000 SF flexible use storage building for F-35 parts, support equipment, shipping/receiving,
and tooling. Storage building will have roll up doors, man doors, lighting, electrical, fire protection, and water. Identified storage space does not meet program
requirements. Current space availability is limited to 40% of required space.

D. Narrative Justification: The amount of projected Carryover for these fiscal years reflects an optimal six-month level to continue mission essential
    performance and fulfill mission requirements. The FRCs continue to monitor and implement measures to mitigate carryover. Assessment of
    material availability, workable work, maximizing optimal work-in-process (WIP) by product line and executing additional Direct Labor Hours to
    burn down aged WIP are examples of on-going efforts to manage carryover across the FRCs. Additionally, working with NAVSUP Weapon System
    Support (WSS), the FRCs have reviewed prior year Aged WIP and returned funding to NAVSUP WSS on work that either is no longer needed or is
    constrained by other factors such as material or carcass constraints. This effort has helped to alleviate the impact to carryover and the potential
    financial NOR loss associated with working items that are fixed price and are not completed in the fiscal year inducted.


    Note: Carryover $ Value by Service & Appropriation - Include orders from other Services and Customers.

                             DEPARTMENT OF THE NAVY
                        SUPPLY MANAGEMENT – MARINE CORPS
                      FISCAL YEAR (FY) 2026 PRESIDENT’S BUDGET
                                       June 2025

Mission Statement/Overview:
The Marine Corps, Supply Management Activity Group (MC SMAG) performs inventory
management functions that result in the sale of Secondary Reparable (SecRep) items to support
Department of Defense (DoD), federal, and non-federal warfighting weapon systems sustainment
requirements. Costs related to providing such inventory (material) support to customers are
recouped through the application of stabilized rates that include recovery for cost elements such
as oversight/inventory management and cost required to stock, store, receive, and issue such
assets. MC SMAG is divided into three Budget Projects to organize the financial operation of the
fund.

Budget Project
Retail – Consumable
Wholesale – Depot Level Reparables
Operations – Cost of Operations

Activity Group Composition:                                                      Location
Marine Corps Inventory Control Point                                            Albany, GA

Significant Changes Since the FY 2025 President’s Budget (PB 2025):
In FY 2026, MC SMAG projects inventory growth due to initial issue provisioning stocks of
SecReps for newly fielded weapons systems (i.e., G/ATOR and ACV) over the next few years.
Both FY2025 and FY2026 inventory will be impacted by strategic divestiture actions coupled
with the implementation of deemed cost revaluation.

Financial Profile:

Revenue and Expense:

                        New Orders, Revenue and Expenses ($M)
         $105
          $70

                          FY 2024                     FY 2025                     FY 2026
     New Orders            $87.97                      $89.21                      $84.81
     Revenue               $90.67                      $96.87                      $82.77
     Expense               $79.18                      $94.41                      $96.58

                                     New Orders   Revenue   Expense

Due to ongoing workforce optimization efforts, it is premature for the Department of the Navy to submit
the estimate of NOR and AOR data related to the Deferred Resignation Program (DRP). Estimates will
continue to be refined as the Department continues to assess the DRP's impacts and implications for both
FY 2025 and FY 2026

Net Revenue – FY 2026 Net Revenue projections declined by $14.1 million from FY 2026 primarily
due to reduced customer orders and fielding delays. New equipment fielding delays are mainly
caused by OEMs failing to meet production schedules, which will postpones delivery of new
equipment to the warfighter. The direct induction process initiative has been implemented aimed
at enhancing visibility of demands across the Enterprise thereby increasing revenue at the
Reparable Issue Points (RIPs). The RIPs are the primary Marine Corps customer responsible for
85% of the SMAG’s revenue.

Expenses – The $2.2 million increase in expenses from FY 2025 to FY 2026 is a result of refinements
to the stratification tool. This improvement optimizes demand and forecast accuracy to improve
the overall requirements determination process. Expenses are understated due to Navy
Enterprise Resource Planning (nERP) system logic updates revaluing carcass cost. The
implications of this system update in conjunction with Moving Average Cost (MAC) pricing
variances will be finalized with the implementation of the Deemed Cost initiative.

Wholesale:
FY 2026 reductions in contract authority (CA) from FY 2025 are attributed to delays in fielding
efforts of newly fielded weapon systems. MC SMAG’s operational execution will remain stable
through the direct induction process, increasing the quantity of Wholesale-managed items
requiring repairs.

Operations:
FY 2026 cost of operations stayed steady from FY 2025 to support costs of the modernization
demand forecasting tool. This is partially offset from storage and processing reductions.

Undelivered Orders:
UDOs represent contracts or orders for goods where a liability remains outstanding. Liabilities
clear against the account when material delivers and payments are processed, and vendors
receive payment. The accrual of liability creates an outlay requirement. This is accounted for in




                                                                                                          Narrative
                                           NARRATIVE
                                   DEPARTMENT OF THE NAVY
                              SUPPLY MANAGEMENT – MARINE CORPS
                            FISCAL YEAR (FY) 2026 PRESIDENT’S BUDGET
                                             June 2025

NWCF-SM cash projections. Long lead-time items continue to contribute to a higher level of
UDOs from prior year obligations.
Backorders are items that do not have issuable inventory on the shelf at the time the requisition
was received while contracts could still be in place awaiting delivery for that material.


                        Undelivered Orders and Back Orders ($M)

                     $20

     Undelivered Orders              27.3                    19.4              11.7
     End Period Back Orders          27.7                    16.6               9.3

                                Undelivered Orders   End Period Back Orders

Backorders will continue to decrease in FY 2025 and into FY 2026 due to long lead-time attainment
actions in FY 2024 being delivered during these respective FYs. It is expected that backorders will
continue to decrease consistent with attainment actions, and lead times continue to stay
consistent.

Performance Indicators: Supply Material Availability (SMA) measures the capacity of the
supply chain to respond to customer demand. FY 2024 through FY 2026 reflects the expected
SMA because of deliberate operational and business changes to meet customer demands and
reduce backorders.

IT Solution:
The SMAG program has initiated a modernization effort to enhance demand planning and
forecasting capabilities. The Aircraft Sustainability Module (ASM)/PC STRAT is a stratification
tool which will optimize inventory levels across the enterprise by both quantity and dollar value
to minimize or reduce backorders. This is a significant advancement in backorder management,
and a key capability that will improve effectiveness and efficiency to Wholesale Budget
Stratification.

Mission Statement/Overview:

Naval Supply Systems Command (NAVSUP) is one of Navy’s critical sustainment enablers, directing
complex supply chains delivering vital material, services, and quality-of-life enhancements to our
warfighters, their families, and our joint and allied partners. This budget synchronizes NAVSUP mission
focus of producing high-impact and measurable mission results; aggressively focusing on Fleet operations
and promotes optimal alignment with the Chief of Naval Operations priorities: Warfighting, Warfighter,
and the Foundation that supports them.

Navy Working Capital Fund-Supply Management (NWCF-SM) is the Department of the Navy’s (DON)
readiness enabler, ensuring NAVSUP provides the right material where required, when needed, at the
best cost, which is vital to arming and sustaining the Navy and Marine Corps warfighting units. The
NAVSUP Enterprise mission is to perform supply chain management functions resulting in sufficient
levels of inventory to support established and funded readiness goals. What makes NWCF-SM unique is
the Contract Authority (CA) provided to NAVSUP allowing obligation of funds an acquisition lead-time
prior to future customer requisitions.

Naval Sustainment System - Supply (NSS-S) is driving coordinated efforts to improve the overall Surface
and Submarine readiness and material availability to support Fleet requirements, execution of CNO
Maintenance Availabilities, reduce current unfilled customer orders (UCO), and increase supply material
availability (SMA). Through planning and modeling, including utilization of Sales and Operations
Planning (S&OP) business decision framework, the NAVSUP budget aligns with the anticipated customer
demands early enough to allow for material production and delivery times, having inventory available
when the customer orders are received. The resulting sales of delivered material allows NAVSUP to
reinvest, or replenish, inventory for future mission partner orders. Deferring, cutting, or accelerating
mission partner requirements places tremendous strain on the NWCF supply system to provide the right
material successfully at the right time.

NAVSUP manages the following Budget Projects (BPs) to organize the financial operations of NWCF-SM:

 Wholesale
  Aviation Consumables
  Ship Repairable and Consumables
  Aviation Repairables

 Retail
   Ship’s Store & Consumables



 Operations and Reimbursables

Significant changes since the FY 2025 President’s Budget (PB 2025):

The Virginia Class (VACL) Material Strategy is an initiative to buy critical initial spare parts in support of
VACL submarine Extended Dry-Dock Selected Restricted Availabilities (EDSRA) and Depot
Modernization Periods (DMP). This financial investment provides for an enduring increase of material on-
hand at the beginning of each VACL EDSRA and DMP and reduces Days of Maintenance Delay (DoMD)
by an estimated 100-111 days, generating ~$100 million in DoMD cost avoidance per year, and returns our
VACL submarines to the Fleet sooner. Based on the lead times of materials, it is anticipated to see the
full benefits of these procurements for Avails starting in FY26 and out. NAVSUP has obligated $909
million towards the VACL material initiative.

NAVSUP, in partnership with OPNAV, is implementing targeted spares initiatives to improve readiness
across aviation, surface, and subsurface. The NAVSUP goal through this budget is to drive Fleet Readiness
by minimizing the number of non-mission capable ships to zero by the end of FY 2026. Surface readiness
efforts focus on Operational Availability (Ao) by utilizing updated RBS models and Amphibious Reset
Steam and Diesel BOM initiative to reduce maintenance delays for aging amphibious ships. Subsurface
readiness includes ongoing Virginia Class (VACL) BOM and Depot SUBCAL for Baseline I-III VACL
submarines. Aviation readiness is supported with updated Wartime Utilization Rates (WUR) to enhance
spares availability and the “Return to Green” (RTG) campaign that aims to bring all 20 Type Model Series
(TMS) platforms that NAVSUP manages to the 80% MC North Star readiness requirement and is expected
to be realized by FY 2027.

Fleet-wide improvements are also driven by the COSAL Demand Model Expansion (DME), which reduces
financial constraints and expands critical repair parts to decrease NMC-S off-ship requisitions. Forward
positioning is strengthened by increasing high-demand materials on Forward Deployed Load Lists (FDLL)

and establishing subsurface load lists to support SRF-W VACL Block III submarines, with specific
attention to submarine configurations rotating out of Australia.

Wholesale:

FY 2026 CA decreased by $468.115 million from FY 2025 mainly driven by commercial procurement and
repair for Aviation Procurement and Repair (BP85). FY 2026 decrease is due to requirements that were
reapportioned from FY 2024 to FY 2025 due to contract constraints. These requirements are projected to
be completed FY 2025 and will not be carried forward into FY 2026. FY 2025, CA funding increased by
$887.5 million from PB 2025 to support submarine and surface ship requirements along with aviation
repairable across the Future Years Defense Program (FYDP).

Retail:

FY 2026 CA increased by $38 million from FY2025 in support of Submarine Wholeness (Shipyards)
increased requirements and DLA/GSA price increase.

Operations:

FY 2026 CA decreased by $143 million from FY 2025 budgeted figures, driven by DLA requirements and
workload.

Wholesale:

Gross sales are directly aligned to customer demands and funding profiles, as well as NAVSUP’s ability
to fill orders utilizing in-stock material and spot-buys after receipt of customer requisition.

FY2026 – Increase of $772.6 million from FY 2025 projections was driven by Aviation projected gross sales
increases of $814.7 million and offset by Maritime projected sales decreases of $42.0 million, driven by a
lag in basic business sales. Aviation drivers for projected sales increases include Outfitting and Special
Program sales along with an FY 2025 forecast that is lower than expected.

Retail:

Increase in retail as sales changes corresponds with obligations.

Undelivered Orders (UDOs) ($M):

UDOs represent contracts or orders for goods where a liability remains outstanding. Liabilities clear
against the NWCF-SM account when material delivers and payments are processed, and vendors receive
payment. The accrual of liability creates an outlay requirement. This is accounted for in NWCF-SM cash

                                              JUNE 2025

projections. Long lead-time items continue to contribute to a higher level of UDOs from prior year
obligations.

Backorders are items that do not have issuable inventory on the shelf at the time the requisition was
received while contracts could still be in place awaiting delivery for that material.

Performance Indicators:

Performance indicators establish the expected level of performance for supply management and measures
the capacity of the supply chain to respond to customer demand. Supply Material Availability is a
NAVSUP Metric that measures the capacity of the supply chain to respond to customer demand.

Unit Cost (UC):
The cost per unit sold includes Wholesale, Retail, and Operations obligations divided by Wholesale,
Retail, and Operations net sales. Unit cost can change in the year of execution.

       Equipment, Non-ADPE*/Telecom           $2.00                 $2.00                 $2.00
       Total                                 $13.00                $27.00                $13.00


The Capital Investment Program sustains NAVSUP in mission achievement by reinvesting in plant
equipment, cranes, information technology (IT), and facilities. Increased information technology
investment continues to enhance analytical capabilities and inventory accuracy. Urgent IT requirements
involving AI projects were prioritized and received an infusion of $14 million from NWCF for FY 2025 but
are expected to return to steady-state in FY 2026.

FY24 POTF *
    * POTF (Percentage of Time Free) is an accepted Department of Defense readiness metric and is used in assessing ship and
   submarine readiness vice NMCS (aviation metric). It measures the percentage of operating time free of mission-degrading
    casualties for active ships in all fleets (i.e. the percentage of operating time that a platform has no C3/C4 casualty reports
(CASREPs). POTF is measured by platform. There is no means of obtaining POTF data at the Weapon System level. POTF DATA

      * POTF (Percentage of Time Free) is an accepted Department of Defense readiness metric and is used in
  assessing ship and submarine readiness vice NMCS (aviation metric). It measures the percentage of operating
 time free of mission-degrading casualties for active ships in all fleets (i.e. the percentage of operating time that a
    platform has no C3/C4 casualty reports (CASREPs). POTF is measured by platform. There is no means of
                                 obtaining POTF data at the Weapon System level.

                                                                                                               Exhibit Fund-9A Capital Investment Summary
Narrative Justification: This exhibit will provide detailed justification by line item in support of summary capital investment purchases shown on the Fund-9a Exhibit.
    -     Describe the enhancement afforded by the existing equipment/ADPE and telecommunications resources/software development/facility and the shortcomings inherent in the current situation.
    -     Describe the benefits to be realized from the proposed capital investment.
    -     Indicate whether an economic analysis or cost analysis has been performed and, if not, why not. Summarize the net present value advantages of the proposed investment over alternatives
          considered and discarded. Be prepared to provide a copy of supporting economic analysis upon request.
    -     For MILCON projects, provide a copy of the supporting Form 1391 for new projects not previously submitted or identified.
    -     Describe the impact of not making the proposed capital investment.
    -     For computer software, separately identify license fees.
                -     Alternatively, dollars in millions may be used out to three decimal places
Column Entries
    A. Element of Cost. For items purchased under the Project/Line Item, provide applicable subcategories (e.g. vehicles may be broken down into cars, trucks, buses, etc.). For Software provide the
          item, and if applicable, break into module delivery subcategories.
    B. Quantity. Provide the approximate number of items to be purchased under the subcategory or as applicable for software.
    C. Per Unit Cost. Enter the actual or estimated unit cost, when appropriate, for each element listed. Express unit costs in thousands of dollars, to the nearest tenth (i.e., $20.1 thousand). Unit
          costs should be expressed in terms of “then year” costs.
    D. Guidance on Unspecified Minor Construction Thresholds

10 U.S. Code § 2805 - Unspecified minor construction
(a) Authority to Carry Out Unspecified Minor Military Construction Projects.— (1)Within an amount equal to 125 percent of the amount authorized by law for such purpose, the Secretary
concerned may carry out unspecified minor military construction projects not otherwise authorized by law.
(2)An unspecified minor military construction project is a military construction project that has an approved cost equal to or less than $3,000,000. However, if the military construction project is
intended solely to correct a deficiency that is life-threatening, health-threatening, or safety-threatening, an unspecified minor
military construction project may have an approved cost equal to or less than $4,000,000.
(d) Laboratory Revitalization.— (1)For the revitalization and recapitalization of laboratories owned by the United States and under the jurisdiction of the Secretary concerned, the Secretary concerned
may obligate and expend— (A)from appropriations available to the Secretary concerned for operation and maintenance, amounts necessary to carry out an unspecified minor military construction
project costing not more than $4,000,000, notwithstanding subsection (c); or
(B)from appropriations available to the Secretary concerned for military construction not otherwise authorized by law or from funds authorized to be made available under section 219(a) of the Duncan
Hunter National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2009 (Public Law 110–417; 10 U.S.C. 2358 note), amounts necessary to carry out an unspecified minor military construction project costing
not more than $4,000,000.
(2)For purposes of this subsection, an unspecified minor military construction project is a military construction project that (notwithstanding subsection (a)) has an approved cost equal to or less than
$4,000,000. The Secretary of Defense shall establish procedures for the review and approval of requests from the Secretary of a military department to carry out a construction project under this
subsection.
(3)Not later than February 1, 2014, the Secretary of Defense shall submit to the congressional defense committees a report on the use of the authority provided by this subsection. The report shall include
a list and description of the construction projects carried out under this subsection, including the location and cost of each project.
(4)In this subsection, the term “laboratory” includes— (A)a research, engineering, and development center; and
(B)a test and evaluation activity.
(5)The authority to carry out a project under this subsection expires on September 30,
2018.

        CAPITAL INVESTMENT JUSTIFICATION                                                             FISCAL YEAR (FY) 2026 PRESIDENT'S BUDGET
             (DOLLARS IN MILLIONS)                                                                                  JUNE 2025
Department of the Navy/     #001 - Non-ADPE                                                                                                 Supply Management - Navy
Supply
                                             FY 2024                                    FY 2025                                                        FY 2026
Non-ADP Equipment             Quant       Unit Cost     Total Cost         Quant         Unit Cost       Total Cost        Quant                 Unit Cost                 Total Cost
 Vehicles                             0       -                  $0.00                0      -                 $500.00                 0             -                                   $500.00
 Material Handling                    0       -                $831.00                0      -               $1,000.00                 0             -                                  $1,000.00
 Installation Security                0       -                  $0.00                0      -                   $0.00                 0             -                                      $0.00
 Quality Control/ Testing             0       -                  $0.00                0      -                   $0.00                 0             -                                      $0.00
 Medical Equipment                    0       -                  $0.00                0      -                   $0.00                 0             -                                      $0.00
 Machinery                            0       -                  $0.00                0      -                 $500.00                 0             -                                   $500.00
 Support Equipment                    0       -                  $0.00                0      -                   $0.00                 0             -                                      $0.00
Total                                 0       -                $831.00                0      -               $2,000.00                 0             -                                     $2,000
Justification:

This program funds the procurement of new/initial outfitting and replacement of Material Handling Equipment (MHE) and Automated Material Handling Systems (AMHS) to satisfy
operational requirements within the Navy Supply System. Replacement MHE is for over aged non-repairable equipment used in material handling operations at various activities. With
a large inventory of equipment at the various Fleet Logistics Centers (FLCs) there will always be units eligible for replacement through procurement. If fully supported, this funding will
allow the Navy to develop the right mix of new procurements, resulting in overall requirement reductions, and resolving the problem of trying to maintain old equipment at high
maintenance cost and reduced state of readiness. MHE funding limitations in past years has precluded the purchase of required MHE planned for issue. We cannot emphasize enough
that this is a continuing program and one year builds on the next. Delaying any funding only postpones the inevitable requirement to procure a new unit at a higher cost. Supply readiness
and logistical support are dependent upon the availability of reliable MHE. Non-repairable equipment is not cost effective to maintain for continued operation, and repair parts are
difficult to obtain. Replacement of non-repairable equipment with new and more efficient models will reduce excessive costs attributed to repair/overhaul, downtime and maintenance.
New equipment will enhance productivity and enable users to meet handling and logistics requirements in an efficient and effective manner. For these reasons it is essential to maintain
funding to cover procurement of new equipment as required.
Naval Supply Systems Command (NAVSUP) is also responsible for replacing and maintaining aging Civil Engineering Support Equipment (CESE) necessary for fuel depot operations
throughout the Navy. This equipment is necessary to maintain and improve the working conditions and assist NAVSUP operations employees. Safety, reliability, maintenance cost and
customer support are directly impacted by age and condition of this equipment. Economic analysis is not provided since equipment is only replaced as useful life has been exceeded due
to age and or usage. Dollar values are established by NAVFAC procuring activity in Port Hueneme, CA. Examples: Tanker truck, 20 ton semi-trailer stake 2 axle, 20 ton semi-trailer
van 2 axle.

   Computer Hardware (Network)                                  0        -            $6,460.00             0        -           $10,000.00                0        -            $10,000.00
   Computer Software (Operating System)                         0        -                 $0.00            0        -                 $0.00               0        -                  $0.00
   Telecommunications                                           0        -                 $0.00            0        -                 $0.00               0        -                  $0.00

Justification:

NAVSUP Business Systems Center (BSC) - Funds provide support to the BSC Legacy/Non-Navy/Marine Corps Intranet (NMCI) Network Plan. As part of the plan, NAVSUP BSC is
continually upgrading its NETWARCOM approved legacy network, which will replace obsolete non-NMCI ADP equipment to provide an environment for client/server development. A
variety of PC hardware platforms currently exists in NAVSUP BSC that prevents deployment of the development tools needed to maintain its competitiveness. Upgrading and
standardizing hardware infrastructure will allow NAVSUP BSC to use the network to deploy the latest legacy/non-NMCI software products. As NAVSUP moves forward with reducing
system and Information Technology (IT) costs and improving business processes, a critical area identified for analysis is Allowancing. In order to optimize the allowance systems and align
with key Enterprise efforts such as Navy ERP and Single Supply Baseline (SSB), NAVSUP continues to streamline current Readiness Suite and Re-Engineering Maritime Allowance
Development (ReMAD) systems via merging the associated databases, standardizing data validations rules and leveraging synergies resulting from combining the platforms. This effort
will position NAVSUP to respond to future Enterprise integration/transition requirements. Increased execution here reflects increased information technology investment to enhance
analytical capabilities and inventory accuracy.

Justification:

Minor Construction: NAVSUP, as the maintenance UIC for all facilities occupied and operated by NAVSUP employees, is responsible for Real Property Maintenance (Minor Construction
portion) of facilities occupied and operated. These NWCF Supply Management projects are necessary to maintain and improve the working conditions for NAVSUP employees. Projects
include Minor Construction requirements of facilities as well as Quality of Life and correction of Safety deficiencies. Minor Construction funding requested supports the overall RPM
objectives of the NAVFAC recommended spending limits of between 2% to 4% annually based on the associated property values. Economic analysis are not performed since Minor
Construction funding limits keep investment percentage to such a small percentage of the total facility value. Cost savings if identified are provided as part of the project documentation
developed. No minor construction project exceeds the current MILCON threshold.

                             DEPARTMENT OF THE NAVY
                           RESEARCH AND DEVELOPMENT
                      FISCAL YEAR (FY) 2026 PRESIDENT’S BUDGET
                                      JUNE 2025

Mission Statement and Overview:
The Navy Working Capital Fund’s (NWCF) Research and Development (R&D) business
provides research, development, test, evaluation, integration, and engineering services to its
customers. The R&D business includes five Naval Warfare Centers and the Naval Research
Laboratory and provides expertise in land, air, sea, space, and information warfare domains.
Each R&D activity makes major contributions to lethality and readiness within the
Department of Navy (DON) and Department of Defense (DOD) with contributions in areas
like battle-space awareness, net-centric operations (connectivity and interoperability), cyber
warfighting capability, test and evaluation of Major Defense Acquisition Programs (MDAPs),
and battle management systems. Continued success by our Warfare Centers and Laboratories
is vital to maintaining and improving upon the mission capabilities of the operating forces that
sustain our global presence.

      Naval Information Warfare Centers (NIWCs) provide Naval, Joint, and National
       knowledge superiority through quality Research, Development, Test, and Evaluation
       (RDT&E); to rapidly deploy and provide full cycle support for sustainable, survivable,
       and interoperable Command, Control, Communication, Computers, Intelligence,
       Surveillance, and Reconnaissance (C4ISR).
      Naval Air Warfare Center (NAWC) provides R&D, engineering, test and evaluation of
       all Navy and Marine Corps aircraft, aircraft systems, weapons and weapon systems.
       NAWC also operates test ranges, test facilities, laboratories and aircraft in support of
       military operations worldwide
      Naval Surface Warfare Center (NSWC) cohesively and seamlessly operates the Navy's
       full spectrum research, development, test and evaluation, engineering, and fleet
       support centers for offensive and defensive systems associated with surface and mine
       warfare combat systems.
      Naval Undersea Warfare Center (NUWC) operates the Navy's full-spectrum research,
       development, test and evaluation, engineering, and Fleet support center for
       submarines, autonomous underwater systems, and offensive and defensive weapon
       systems associated with Undersea Warfare (USW).
      Naval Research Laboratory (NRL) operates as the Navy's full-spectrum corporate
       laboratory, conducting a broadly based multidisciplinary program of scientific
       research and advanced technological development directed toward maritime
       applications of new and improved materials, techniques, equipment, systems and
       ocean, atmospheric, and space sciences and related technologies.
      Naval Facilities Engineering and Expeditionary Warfare Center (EXWC) operates
       Navy’s research, development, test and evaluation for support combatant capabilities
       and sustainable facilities through specialized engineering, technology development,
       and lifecycle logistics services. As a member of the Naval Facilities Engineering
       Command (NAVFAC) and a designated Science and Technology Reinvention
       Laboratory (STRL), EXWC provides worldwide support services to the Navy, Marine
       Corps and other Department of Defense (DoD) agencies.

Significant Changes since the FY 2025 President’s Budget:

FY 2026 budget includes a decrease in FTEs/workforce aligning with DON’s overall effort to
optimize resource allocation across the government. It also continues to include cost
associated with China Lake Earthquake for major equipment procurements including
temporary facilities and damaged equipment.

FY 2026 budget also includes deferrals for Navy’s Energetics Comprehensive Modernization
Plan (ECMP), approved by ASN(RDA) in 2023. ECMP will unlock the Organic Industrial
Base’s latent capacity, while committing to capability/capacity modernization over the
mid/long-term. NISE investment for FY25 is $591 million and $587 million for FY26.
Surcharges are performed in accordance with the 10 USC 2363 to fund laboratory
revitalization and recapitalization projects in that year.

FY 2026 includes a slight decrease in orders based on forecasted customer demand. Changes
in revenue are due to the removal of the pay raise and partial offsets by Capital Surcharges in
FY 2024, 2025 and 2026. In addition, the capital surcharges in FY 2024, FY 2025, and FY
2026 support vital Capital Investment Program (CIP) projects and support additional Naval
Innovative Science and Engineering (NISE) investments for Defense Laboratory
Revitalization Program (LRP) that exceed capital investment recovery.

The Unit Cost is an expense rate method established to authorize and control costs. Unit cost
goals allow activities to respond to workload changes in execution by encouraging reduced
costs when workload declines and allowing appropriate increases in costs when customers
request additional services. FY 2026 unit cost reflects stabilized costs per associated
stabilized hours as an expense rate.

The Stabilized Rate consists of direct labor and applied overhead. Unique direct non-labor
costs are billed on a reimbursable basis to the customer. The composite rate change
incorporates both the stabilized costs and the reimbursable costs. The composite rate change
in FY 2026 reflects adjustments to direct workload, pricing changes, and increases.

The Capital Investment Program allows the NWCF to achieve its mission by reinvesting in
plant equipment and facilities. Included in the capital budget are the following types of assets:
Automated Data Processing Equipment (ADPE), non-ADPE equipment, software, and minor
construction. Minor construction includes projects meeting the criteria of the Defense
Laboratory Revitalization Program (DLRP). FY 2026 major projects include: Airborne
Networking Lab Expansion which provides a centralized and consolidated lab facility for the
Airborne Networks Team which is currently spread over nine buildings; South Point Lab
Expansion which increases classified laboratory space to support Communications and
Network Department's research, development, and testing; and St. Julien's Creek New Lab
and Warehouse which supports new secure spaces.


Direct Appropriation:

In FY 2026, NWCF R&D estimates include $382 million direct appropriation for Navy’s
Energetics Comprehensive Modernization Plan (ECMP), Organic Industrial Base (OIB).

Justification: NAWC

Pre-investment economic analyses were performed for all investments.

FY 2024

SAIL Network Tactical Common Data Link (NTCDL)
The Surface/Aviation Interoperability Laboratory (SAIL) facility provides programs with an up front and early exposure to deployed naval
systems and capabilities that provide risk reduction and cost efficiency for customers. SAIL has a requirement to provide realistic and shipboard
representative data links to support the Integration, Interoperability, and Developmental Testing of Tactical Data Link. Naval aviation assets
utilize common data links systems (CDLS) to pass sensor data as well as voice and command and control information, and video to shipboard
assets in order to support surface force missions. The current CDLS located at SAIL will become obsolete with the baselines in the fleet.
SAIL’s outdated CDLS system is not able to implement all of the 15 different waveforms, with five simultaneous links, which may be
transmitted and received from all variants of CDL-equipped aircraft. This project will procure, install, and integrate a NTCDL system.
Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

Ordnance Integration Support Team (OIST) Mass Property Instrument Equipment
The Ordnance Integration Support Team provides mass property measurements for all NAE flight test programs. Mass Property
measurements/data are required prior to and in support of all NAE Air Vehicle Stores Compatibility captive carriage and weapons separation test
events. OIST’s Mass Properties Machine is used to provide 3-axis center of gravity and moment of inertia measurements for multiple air vehicle
                                                                                                             Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
stores and munition types. The existing Mass Properties Machine was procured in 2008 and is reaching the end of its service life. This project
will procure a new Mass Properties Machine. This project will procure upgraded simulator capabilities. Alternatives have been considered,
however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

Fiber Optics & Photonics Lab – 100Gb+ Capability
The NAWCAD Fiber Optics & Photonics Lab (FOPL) develops, tests and evaluates high speed fiber optic network components as well as
network protocols. In addition, this lab assesses component performance of both wave division and message passing networks/links and
evaluates component failures and provides technical support. Conducting fiber optics and photonics systems research, development, test
and evaluation (RDT&E) is a primary function of NAWCAD’s mission IAW NAVAIRINST 5451.65B. 100Gb+ Fiber Optics Capability is a
rapidly growing standard that is not currently supported in the FOPL. The 100Gb+ capability along with current and future data requirements for
naval platforms are requiring increasingly greater bandwidths and while innovations are occurring, the FOPL does not have the ability to verify,
validate, nor provide end-to-end testing of any current Fiber Optics projects, components, or assets due to lack of required test equipment. This
project will procure the 100Gb+ capability. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost effective solution for the
government.

Hive Drone Swarms
The NAWCAD Unmanned Autonomy and Robotics Team (UART) supports experimentation, research, and development of Advanced
Unmanned Technologies for Unmanned Aircraft Systems (UAS). This project will procure Robotic Hives ISO to address this current testing
capability shortfall. The Hive is a fully automated UAS ground management platform, designed to make UAS adoption and usage push-button
simple. It is a system that automates the entire operational cycle for heterogenous teams of UAS including: storage, launch, recovery, power
management, and strategic coordination to enable persistent operations. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost
effective solution for the government.

MATERIALS ENGINEERING LAB
The Materials lab contains old equipment and is missing equipment that is needed to test modern materials. This antiquity leads to prolonged
downtime and the inability to support the Navy in current material needs. The computer systems in the lab are outdated, run slowly, and do not
integrate well with newer software. The Instron test frame has no ability to measure extended gauge lengths and limited ability to measure gauge
lengths. Current microscopy systems are low resolution and have low precision and accuracy. Current missing or outdated systems lead to longer
lead times and less accurate results.

CASTING OVEN FACILITY
The need for preheating of assets prior to energetics cast, and the need to cure energetic assets after cast. Additionally, many of the assets are of
a new generation, demonstrating future weapons capability; they require a substantial increase in complexity to set up, precast assembly and post
cast curing. With such, it is imperative the precast preheating and the post cast curing occurs at a location that is very close in proximity to the
actual location of the cast operation. This oven would support many current R&D programs; however, it would be the most beneficial to larger

                                                                                                                Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
rocket motors implementing the High Level Grain (HLG) technology, or future weapons capability demonstration programs. Additionally,
programs in direct support of the fleet such as JMEWS would benefit greatly due to the requirement of preheating.

CRYSTALS, THIN FILMS, AND MATERIALS STRUCTURAL CHARACTERIZATION LABORATORY
Improved analytical equipment to service various missions of NAWCWD, the DoN, and the broader DoD.
This proposal integrates nine instruments integral to maintaining and supporting active research projects, enabling future opportunities, and
providing necessary support across a variety of DoD customers. These projects include novel energetics, advances in fuels from renewable
sources and for hypersonic, coatings, and new materials.
We require new systems, as noted below, in order to maintain these capabilities to support ongoing projects and to attract new work and sponsors
in the future. In addition updating this capability will enable us to partner more effectively with other researchers across DoD, industry and
academia.

DIGITAL TWIN INFRASTRUCTURE (2nd Year)
  - This project is to procure and setup a digital twin infrastructure for shared usage by customers.
  - Digital Twin potential for shorter design development timeline and reduced risk in digital algorithm development prior to CDR could be
    achieved by starting digital firmware/software development and validation in a representative digital environment much earlier than could
    be achieved in a traditional “heel to toe” program constrained by long lead and target hardware build timelines.
  - Currently software and detailed algorithm development usually cannot happen until hardware is locked down as well as throughput
    limitations based on hardware stability. This infrastructure has the ability to reduce 20% of a programs schedule, thereby also reducing
    cost. Additionally, it is much cheaper to have multiple iterations of the digital twin to use in various environments that require high
    fidelity representation but not the actual hardware; ex. trainers, flight simulators, and modeling environments.

ADVANCED OPTICAL RECEIVER LABORATORY FACILITY
Threat detection range is a key operational requirement for EW systems operating at extreme ranges. A recent commercial breakthrough in
electro-optic modulators can deliver a 2x-5x improvement in the detection range of EW receivers by just changing the RF font end of the
receiver to an RF over fiber architecture. EA-18G, P-8. And JSF have all recently sponsored S&T projects to adapt this new technology to their
receivers. NAVAIR just awarded 2 SBIRs one for a ruggedized version of the new EO modulator, and a direct to phase 2 to explore RF over
Fiber receiver architectures for the ALQ-218 (image to the right). NAWCWD lacks the facilities to test and evaluate RF over Fiber receiver
components and systems.

ANECHOIC CHAMBER REFURBISHMENT
All Flight Test System (FTS) antennas must undergo 100% testing for Voltage Standing Wave Ratio (VSWR) and radiation patterns per RCC-
319. Telemetry ™ and Global Positioning System (GPS) antennas that are designed by Air Vehicle Modification and Instrumentation (AVMI)
undergo pattern testing and VSWR to verify conformance to specifications. AVMI is seeking to maintain this capability in testing conformal
telemetry/flight termination/GPS antennas that radiate from P to C-Band. With the deteriorating absorber material from the 1980’s, there is a
need to refurbish the anechoic chamber. This need is becoming more prevalent due to the current fire safety regulations and the degrading
performance of the current anechoic chamber.

 FARM B2964 Chamber Replacement

considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

Distributed Operations UxS Ground System (DOUGS) Farm
There is an increasing number of UAS platforms supporting the Navy’s Air Wing of the Future (AWOF). All platforms currently have their own
RF shelters and Antenna Towers to support Line of Sight (LOS) operations. This inefficiently consumes valuable space on the airfield, leaving
limited capacity for future grown of UxS operations at Pax River.
This DOUGS Farm project will provide a Radio Frequency (RF) Shelter that will connect to multiple Antenna Tower(s) with a secure
connection between program equipment and will be dual accredited up to TS-SCI and SAP. Alternatives have been considered, however this
project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.
