 FY 2026

NAWC-38 Vessel Replacement
NAWCAD Atlantic Targets and Marine Operations (ATMO) has a Key West mission that supports RDT&E and Fleet Training with maritime
support services. Services include: deployment and recovery of Unmanned Systems, acoustic systems, underwater test article recovery, Full
Ship Shock Trials (FSST), Combat System Ship Qualification Trials (CSSQT), salvage operations, fleet training, and the deployment and
recovery of sea and aerial targets. This mission is currently supported by a 192’ offshore supply vessel (NAWC-38) that is 43 years old and
beyond its service life. This project will procure a replacement vessel. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-
effective solution for the government.

 DETONATION MECHANCIS 2.0: ADVANCING THE STANDARDS
Detonation Mechanics has produced advanced explosive technology since the Manhattan Project. Around the mid-2000s, this facility was
incapable of maintaining these high standards due to personnel turnover, structural longevity, operation degradation, and outdated data systems.
Over the past 15 years, there has been personnel development and $4M in structural longevity upgrades. It is now time to update the facility
operation and data systems to make Detonation Mechanics the state-of-the-art facility it was so well known for.

SURFACE MOUNT TECHNOLOGY
  • The objective is to replace the outdated SMT machines that has limited capabilities, produce inconsistent defective printed circuit board
    and are becoming increasingly costly to use that severely restricts our ability to produce high quality product to our customers.
  • We need this fully automated SMT machines to produce high quality printed circuit boards, that will reduce cost, greatly improve
    schedule and reduce waste/scrap components and PCB.
  • The deficiency will address the high labor cost of manual rework, poor quality, downtime and on time deliverables.

QUALITY CONTROL/TESTING

Investments support diagnostic analysis, fault identification, failure analysis, testing and calibration for ship components. Products typically
include electronic modules, circuit cards, power supplies, displays, assemblies and sub-assemblies of shipboard machinery and components.
Quality Control/Assurance and Testing investments provide the Navy reliable processes and procedures to ensure technical specifications and
functional requirements meet developed product/service standards. The identification of unit failures and poor service results in corrective action
designed to improve the production or service process being measured to achieve the desired mission results. Investments provide for quality
control/assurance and test results that are accurate and emulate shipboard environments, which eliminates the need to schedule shipboard testing
and quickens the retest of ships systems. Failure to make these investments may result in economically inefficient operations, unreliable test
results, or human casualties. All non-ADPE Quality Control/Testing projects have an estimated useful life of 10 years and an average payback
period of 5.8 years.

mounting/adjusting system for more accurate tooling alignment. 2. Increase ram force from 25 tons to 32+ tons. 3. Add integrated load cell for
better process control. 4. Add a new updated gravimetric feeding system which will increase the rate of production. 5. Add a new updated

control system to eliminate downtime. These upgraded features will improve the quality of pellets produced with smaller tolerance range and
increase productivity by reducing downtime. The payback period for this investment is 2.3 years.

FY25 Annealing Oven Process Water Cleaning System Replacement– $1,450K (NSWC Indian Head; Indian Head, MD) - This project
will replace the two existing, but obsolete, photocatalytic reactors at the unique double-base propellant grain annealing oven complex located in
the Extrusion Plant. New reactors will be state-of-the-art custom configured versions that are three times more powerful, include smart controls
that report the condition of the UV lamps, quartz lamp tubes and ballasts back to the control system, and utilize non-fouling catalyst isolation
filtration and microbubble reaction air addition. Also includes a mineral salt removal and pH control system to replace the facility’s non-
functional steam still as the dissolved solids handling system. The payback period for this investment is 4.1 years.

FY26 Portable SCIF for Intelligent Autonomous Systems R&D- $1,284K (NSWC Crane; Crane, IN) – The overall objective of the

Munitions Division (JXR). Growth opportunities within the Warfighter community have driven JXR to increase capability and workload aligned
with the Special Warfare and Expeditionary Systems Department (SWESD) strategic positioning objectives for Intelligent Autonomous Systems
(IAS) and System of Systems Test and Evaluation (SoS T&E). The scope of the proposed project includes the site preparation, acquisition and
installation of a portable Sensitive Compartmented Information Facility (SCIF), Electronic Security Systems (ESS) installation and
communications infrastructure (data and voice). Key attributes of the facility include a 20 feet by 50 feet portable structure in compliance with
SCIF security requirements that will provide conference / lab area, two office spaces, and NIPR (9) / SIPR (4) / JWICS (4) drops to
accommodate data processing, modeling and simulations (M&S), SVTC, and data / voice communications.

capability complements the x-ray microscope (XRM) system and offers significant improvements to the existing micro-CT x-ray system. New,
Rotating Target technology offers increased x-ray penetration without sacrificing ultimate resolution. The payback period for this investment is
6.3 years.

MATERIAL HANDLING

N/A

QUALITY CONTROL/TESTING

Investments support diagnostic analysis, fault identification, failure analysis, testing and calibration for ship components. Products typically
include electronic modules, circuit cards, power supplies, displays, assemblies and sub-assemblies of shipboard machinery and components.
Quality Control/Assurance and Testing investments provide the Navy reliable processes and procedures to ensure technical specifications and
functional requirements meet developed product/service standards. The identification of unit failures and poor service results in corrective action
designed to improve the production or service process being measured to achieve the desired mission results. Investments provide for quality
control/assurance and test results that are accurate and emulate shipboard environments, which eliminates the need to schedule ship board testing
and quickens the retest of ships systems. Failure to make these investments may result in economically inefficient operations, unreliable test
results, or human casualties. All non-ADPE Quality Control/Testing projects have an estimated useful life of 10 years and an average payback
period of 5.8 years.

combat systems and ensures that research and development achieves proper and accurate test results. Equipment supporting this mission
includes explosive detection equipment, ship hull test equipment, seafloor/sub-floor sonar imaging equipment, and test and evaluation equipment
for various surface ship systems. The Naval Surface Warfare Center activities are responsible for new product testing as well as system in-
service engineering. Failure to make these investments may result in work that produces obsolete results to the scientific community,
economically inefficient operations and possible risk to human life. All non-ADPE support equipment projects have an estimated useful life of
10 years, and the average payback period is 5.1 years.

PROJECTS UNDER $1M

The “Amada Punch Press machine” project in FY25 provides enhanced manufacturing support for Research and Development (R&D),
production, and casualty report (CASREP) repairs of mission critical subsystems. The purchase and installation of the new 33-ton punch press
will enable larger material handling, thicker material punching, and faster production. The previous punch press was manufactured 38 years ago
and is more than a decade past its life expectancy. It is unserviceable due to its age and lack of replacement components. If not funded, robust
capability improvements will be unrealized, and the risk of catastrophic failure increases with age.

                                                                                                             Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
Justification: NRL

Support Equipment
Capital investment in the support equipment capability will preserve, enhance and support requirements to maintain a technologically advanced,
state-of-the-art laboratory and is tied directly to NRL's science and technology (S&T) mission. Investments cover a broadly based multi-
disciplinary program of scientific research and advanced technological development directed toward maritime applications of new and improved
materials, techniques, equipment, systems, and ocean, atmospheric and space sciences and related technologies.

NRL's largest investments in FY 2024 will be, “Confocal Spectroscopic Imaging System “, “NCST High-Temperature Experimental Test
Cell for High Speed Propulsion Research “, and “Multi-Function Laser System (MFLS) “. The “Confocal Spectroscopic Imaging System
“ system enables 25nm lateral resolution for optically interrogating materials down to single particle all in one microscope and includes the
increased ability for in-house research and reduction in external evaluation of materials, devices, and systems. The “NCST High-Temperature
Experimental Test Cell for High Speed Propulsion Research “ system will generate clean, high-temperature, and high-speed air flows
simulating the combustor environment of a vehicle flying at supersonic/hypersonic speeds to allow propulsion testing in a laboratory setting.
This project will naturally bring–in new funding to the NCST and yield a high return on investment for the laboratory as customers retain
systems engineering and subject matter expertise support in addition to patronizing this low-cost, high-throughput test cell. The acquisition of
this CIP purchase will also allow important cost-reduction benefits for internal experimental and computational research programs. The “Multi-
Function Laser System (MFLS) “will collect more precise lunar ranging data for improved understanding of the Moon’s liberations. New
investments into a state-of-the-art high energy short pulsed laser at the OTF would reduce maintenance costs at the OTF and preserve NRL as a
leader in space geodesy and space navigation, enabling R&D into three burgeoning SLR applications: tracking unenhanced space debris (spent
rocket bodies, defunct satellites, etc.) in low earth orbit, lunar ranging with short pulsed laser for development of more precise lunar reference
frames, and tracking enhanced objects in orbital regimes beyond geostationary orbit (lunar, cislunar).

NRL's largest investments in FY 2025 will be, “Robotic Asset Characterization System (RACS) “, “67GHz Electromagnetic Signal
Response and Degradation Analysis Suite“, “MRC Accurate Timing Distribution System (MRC-ATDS)“, and the “North Chamber
Upgrade,” all of which cost more than one million dollars. The “Robotic Asset Characterization System (RACS) “includes hardware and
software, capable of accurate and reproducible payload positioning and orientation. The RACS will enable automated effects testing and robust
characterization of threat sensors. Use of these arms would benefit many sections in NRL as well as collaborative projects across the laboratory.
As we respond to growing, technically complex threats requiring multi-skillset approaches, the importance of placing test articles and
measurement devices in precise physical locations has become evident. This capability is crucial in multiple laboratories and is clearly needed by
the division and NRL in general. Being portable would allow our division to lend out this capability to other divisions. The “67GHz
Electromagnetic Signal Response and Degradation Analysis Suite“ is an essential asset to the Optical Sciences Division (OSD), allowing for

                                                                                                               Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
the precise characterization of analog RF photonic systems. Additionally, it will benefit the Tactical Electronic Warfare Division (TEW),
reducing the workload on their researchers and systems. As the frequency and complexity of potential threats increases, the capabilities of the
OSD must grow to compensate. This system will allow for the photonic hardware designed and built at NRL to continue to meet or surpass the
required specifications. The “MRC Accurate Timing Distribution System (MRC-ATDS)“ allows for accurate and precise timing essential to the
success of NRL's Midway Research Center (MRC). Over the years, NRL has made substantial investments in developing a state-of-the-art
atomic clock reference at MRC to provide precise time and frequency signals to various radio and optical assets across the site. These atomic
clock signals have supported significant R&D in areas critical to national security, enabling MRC to become a leader in advanced signal
generation, processing, and calibration techniques. Maintaining this leading role in the future requires upgrading of the infrastructure that is used
to distribute the clock reference signals to assets onsite but are remote from the clock. This upgrade is needed now to support future R&D
advancements in key areas of the IC, DOD, and DON strategic plans. Lastly, the “North Chamber Upgrade” procurement and installation of
the upgraded pumping system of the North Chamber allows for lower cost maintenance and increases the operating reliability versus the current
system. This also provides opportunities for design optimization. NRL engineers and scientists optimize the designs of their test configurations
based on the in-house capabilities and interfaces of the facility. This optimization affords the ability to eliminate outside contractor services,
simplify integration flows and test procedures, and reduce test configuration complexity. All these factors combine to significantly reduce
program costs and schedules.

NRL's largest investments in FY 2026 will be, “Augmenting Bench & Chamber Measurement Capabilities “, “600 MHz NMR
Spectrometer “, “Optical Modulation Analyzer (OMA) “, and the “North Thermal Vacuum Chamber Upgrade”. The “Augmenting
Bench & Chamber Measurement Capabilities“ asset is a modern systems and surveillance platforms that utilizes sophisticated waveforms,
has higher processing capabilities, and ability to do multimode detections. Counter measures and decoys will need to respond in a multispectral
regime with high fidelity projection in a multimode approach. This augmentation in technology will allow the OCM branch and TEW division to
test and characterize systems with state-of-the-art approaches to meet and anticipate next generation threats, maximizing usage of established
facilities such as the 5715 far field chamber to measure a larger breath device in various modes. The “600 MHz NMR Spectrometer “ will
replace an aging system which has required significant maintenance. This is a critical asset used to determine the molecular structure of materials
nondestructively and it is considered a standard for chemical identification. The “Optical Modulation Analyzer (OMA)” is critical for
developing fiber optic and for enhancing the state-of-the-art in Lasercom and associated mediums for transmission. To give the highest possible
data refresh rate, the OMA software is made to rapidly gather data from the oscilloscope and transfer it into the MATLAB workspace. After that,
MATLAB is used to process the data in order to extract and show the measured results. NRL investment into the OTF has brought unique
capabilities over the years, including supporting NASA, SDA, Space Force, DARPA. The asset offers the potential to support new customers
(e.g., NASA, NGA) as they look forward to enabling lunar space missions with high precision positioning, navigation, and timing (PNT)
capabilities.

                                                                                                                 Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
Lastly, the “North Thermal Vacuum Chamber Upgrade” project is to modify (renovate and upgrade) the vertical lift thermal vacuum (TVAC)
chamber denoted "North Chamber" of the Naval Center for Space Technology's (NCST) Environmental Test Facility to implement facility safety
and performance upgrades. A new vacuum pump and gate valve is in needed repair. The new cryopump has higher pumping capability than the
current pump. Reconfiguring the chamber and system equipment will: 1) reduce the effective evacuated volume by a third, thus reducing pump
down times, meantime between pump regenerations, and overall test durations, 2) provide easy access to equipment for maintenance or repair,
even during testing, and 3) position critical equipment closer to the chamber, thus lessening the loads on the vacuum pumps and the shroud
thermal conditioning unit, thereby enabling improved system performance, reliability and lower operating cost.

Pre-investment economic analyses were performed for all investments.

Justification: EXWC

In FY 2024, EXWC is requesting a Naval Innovative Science and Engineering (NISE) Capital Investment project to modernize and expand the
laboratory's Microgrid Test Bed. The NAVFAC EXWC Microgrid Test Bed laboratory, located at Naval Base Ventura County, Port Hueneme,
provides vital microgrid energy research and modeling capabilities to the Navy and DoD. The Microgrid Test Bed equipment provides the
capability to conduct research from multiple users and projects, inform microgrid infrastructures, and supports microgrid deployment across the
Navy and the DoD to address climate and energy resilience.

The modernization/upgrade will expand the capability of the Microgrid Test Bed to support research and testing of microgrid modeling and
components and the Microgrid Academy to educate Navy and DoD utility professionals and technicians skills needed to design and operate
microgrids. The effort adds generator capability, upgrades switchgear controls, and add lithium-ion battery energy storage.

This need aligns with the Presidential Policy Direction 21 for “the ability to prepare for and adapt to changing conditions and withstand and
recover rapidly from disruptions; and the DoN Climate Action 2030 – 65% reduction of greenhouse gas emission by 2030.

Justification: NAWC

Reprogramming’s

FY 2024

RDT&E Next Generation Firewall Mesh
The NAWCAD RDT&E Enterprise Network supports all current test programs and laboratories /test facilities, by providing the single, protected
data environment for processing and evaluating weapons system test performance on a variety of engineering platforms. This project will
procure new architecture equipment to support next-generation network needs, including IA requirements. Alternatives have been considered,
however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

RDT&E Object Storage
NAWCAD Information Technology (IT) infrastructure, application support, and Information Assurance (IA) services supports an existing object
storage solution on the RDT&E network which is 1 Petabyte on SDREN and 3 Petabytes on DREN. This object storage capability currently
supports multiple flight test programs across NAWCAD and must be maintained to continue to provide the required storage environment.
Existing object storage appliances are End of Life (EoL) as of December 2022 and the vendor is no longer providing operating systems updates.
This proposal addresses equipment obsolescence and will provide a modern and maintained solution to support Flight Test Data and RDT&E
laboratory storage requirements for the Command. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution
for the government.

INTEGRATED FIRES LABORATORY
  - This CIP project is to provide the equipment for Michelson Laboratory Wing 5 after the renovation is complete.

                                                                                                          Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
  -    Wing 5 is currently under renovation and when completed will provide an ICD-705 compliant facility.
  -    Wing 5 will be utilized to house the Integrated Fires Laboratory which is a command initiative that will provide a multi-level security
      environment.
  -    The Integrated Fires Laboratory will include virtual ranges that support multi-mission, multi-domain mission-level analysis and
      integration across the Carrier Strike Group

HPC Clusters (High Performance Computational Cluster Replacement)
 - Several analysis branches perform both testing and M&S
 - M&S supports better understanding of physics-based systems.
 - Higher performance weapons will require more computational predictive analysis in the future.
 - Tests can be better understood or reduced, leading to reduced cost.
 - Two Linux clusters are currently in use by 4 groups.
        - One is obsolete and experiencing hardware failures.
        - One will be obsolete by F24
 - Clusters need to be updated to maintain computing capability.
 - NAWCWD needs to be competitive with other labs and industry.
 - Perform analyses when industry cannot do so.

FY 2025

Cloud Security Stack Replacement (PDSS)
NAWCAD is a Cloud Naval Technical Authority (NTA) that provides access and security for all NTA cloud hosted servers and applications.
The Physical Datacenter Security Stack (PDSS) is a network security boundary which provides geographically redundant, secure access between
U.S. Navy production/research networks (NIPR, DREN) and cloud service providers (CSPs). The current PDSS components which support the
requirement will begin to reach end of life in FY 2026. This project will modernize the PDSS infrastructure. Alternatives have been considered,
however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

Classified Network Refresh
The existing classified RDT&E infrastructure at Patuxent River and Webster Outlying Field (WOLF) is failing to meet the increased
customer demand. An upgrade to the existing classified Patuxent River RDT&E network environment will allow for higher throughput,
increased reliability, and position the infrastructure to meet the new cybersecurity requirements, particularly for Software Defined Access (SDA)
AND Zero-Trust Access (ZTA) support. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the
government.

Unified Communications #2

                                                                                                              Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
Communications networking systems are used to connect the NAWCAD community by providing worldwide access for video and voice to
provide collaborative information sharing and analysis. The existing network infrastructure if outdated and nearing end of life which is raising
concerns with interoperability and the ability to obtain and share information with community partners. Alternatives have been considered,
however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

RDT&E Security Operations Visibility & Automated Response (SOAR)
The NAWCAD Digital Networks and Applications (DNA) Department provides NAWCAD Information Technology (IT) infrastructure,
application support, and Information Assurance (IA) services. The Security Operations Center (SOC) is responsible for managing security
incidents, remediation activities, and proactive monitoring of the RDT&E network. The SOC Team must be able to monitor network security,
prioritize alerts, and provide initial response to those alerts. This project will procure a Security Operations Automated Response system that
will provide additional network security capability. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution
for the government.

INTEGRATED FIRE LABORATORY
  - This CIP project is to provide the equipment for Michelson Laboratory Wing 5 after the renovation is complete
  -  Wing 5 is currently under renovation and when completed will provide an ICD-705 compliant facility
  -  Wing 5 will be utilized to house the Integrated Fires Laboratory which is a command initiative that will provide a multi-level security
    environment
  -  The Integrated Fires Laboratory will include virtual ranges that support multi-mission, multi-domain mission-level analysis and
    integration across the Carrier Strike Group

MIXER PROGRAMMABLE LOGIC CONTROLLER
 - Quality: Need to have immediate backup/ restoring system in case of in operation system fault. Multipoint failure system must be
    instituted for better operator control to preserve energetic in the mixer and minimize material loss.
 -   Industry Match Need: Control systems need to be modernized and standardized with coming MILCONs, which will simplify and lower
    maintenance costs.
 -   Cyber Security: Modern system on modern operating software is needed to meet cyber security requirements. Need to have known
    control system built to specifications given by end users.

MODERNIZED SPECTRUM WAREFARE LABORATORY
 • Laboratories at NAWCWD are operating in a legacy fashion.
 • Inability to make more than sporadic incremental progress in current laboratories due to workloads and prioritization of current delivery
 • Strong prioritization in laboratories for PoR delivery instead of new mission data and planning capabilities, research, and prototyping

                                                                                                              Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
  •   Inability to move beyond SECRET-level accreditation.
  •   Requirement to create a lab where NAWCWD modernizes the capabilities required for future mission data reprogramming, including
      automation, AI/ML, digital twins, threat M&S, and LVC capability.
  •   Requirement to prioritize research tasking, including applied research and prototyping.

DE NETWORK FRAMEWORK FOR UNCLASSIFIED ENGINEERING
 • NAWCWD has invested a lot of time and effort in discussing and planning for conversion to a Digital Engineering (DE) environment,
    with the majority of effort focused on MBSE and higher-level security options. The bulk of baseline engineering work is still done on
    disconnected unclassified RDTE systems with data transfer via sneakernet or discrete file transfer (DoD SAFE).
 • The purpose of this project is to build digital engineering infrastructure to support model-based engineering for design and manufacturing
    of prototype engineering efforts, such as the CHAINSW project.
 • The project will serve as a prototype for future DE environments at WD and will be designed in conjunction with the digital engineering
    office.

AUTONOMY RESEARCH ARENA MODERNIZATION (AURA)
Over a decade ago the Autonomy Research Arena (AuRA) was established at NAWCWD. The acquisition of the then state-of-the-art motion
capture (MOCAP) system and research grade quadcopters played a critical role in the creation of a new research area at NAWCWD providing
essential tools to our scientists and engineers while fostering innovation and development of new algorithms for the warfighter. In order
to ensure relevance and improve speed to the fleet the AuRA needs to be updated.

Justification: NSWC

Pre-investment economic analyses were performed for all investments.

ADP Equipment Computer Hardware (Production)

These investments ensure network connectivity to all Naval Warfare Center activities and procurement of hardware for mission essential
research and development computing needs and centralized system hosting including: business system replacement, technical refresh of
classified clusters, intrusion detection control systems, high speed computing, and research and development. Equipment also supports maritime
modeling, simulation, and testing. Such investments provide technology tools for the research and development community and continuity of
operations for standard business systems throughout the Warfare Center. ADP Equipment supporting the research and development community
must remain on the cutting edge of technology to conduct complex simulations, harness advanced data analytics & machine learning capabilities,
perform predictive analysis, and analyze surface ship system performance. Current equipment supporting mission essential systems will no
longer be supported by the manufacturer. ADPE Computer Hardware Production projects have an estimated useful life of 10 years, and the
average payback period is 4 years.

FY25 Enterprise Backup and Recovery Solution - $2,800K (NUWC Newport; Newport RI) – Procure and integrate the hardware to
provide a state-of-art Enterprise Backup and Recovery solution for both unclassified and classified Research, Development, Test & Evaluation
(RDT&E) domains. This solution will create, manage, offer and deliver enterprise data backup services as efficiently as possible which needs to
be done without impact to compliance or security by providing a backup solution that is hardened and remarkedly less demanding in terms of
configuration complexity and operational manpower when compared to a traditional tape backup system. This solution aligns NUWCNPT with
other WCs and allow collaboration with other WCs to have synchronized backups located at multiple WFCs to address disaster recovery
concerns.

PROJECTS ABOVE $1M

The “Research, Development, Test & Evaluation (RDT&E) Network Upgrade" project in FY24 in the computer hardware (network)
capability would provide a tech refresh/upgrade of RDT&E Network Security infrastructure. Various network devices will be required to
support advances in technology, expansion and new security requirements. Additionally, core infrastructure, Host based Security System
(HBSS) monitoring, and Assured Compliance Assessment Solution (ACAS) scanning servers will continue to be hosted on-site. The RDT&E
network supports technical efforts which support the warfighter. An economic analysis has been performed. Without this investment, the
RDT&E Network infrastructure would remain in its current state with a potential for increased maintenance costs and server outages that would
put the network at risk.

FY26 Research, Development, Test & Evaluation (RDT&E) Private 5G project in FY26 provides the buildout of a 5G RDT&E network in
the Bayside and Topside areas of Naval Information Warfare Center (NIWC) Pacific to enable increased capability for staff to access mission
critical information. An economic analysis will be performed as part of the proposal review process. Cost savings includes nearly $200k in
current copper ethernet and fiber optic that will become unnecessary in covered areas. If the investment is not approved, reconfigured spaces
will continue to require additional funding for design and RDT&E network cabling.

Justification: NRL

Other Support Equipment

In FY 2024, the “(LOBO) Rejuvenating and Enhancing the Navy’s VLITE Asset project” precision measurements of density variations
within Earth’s ionosphere exceed that of commonly used Global Positioning System (GPS) methods by over two orders of magnitude, providing
unmatched tests of global and regional models such as NRL’s SAMI (Sami is Another Model of the Ionosphere). This purchase reduce data gaps
that limit operational efficiency, but it will also yield improved image quality and the ability to detect fainter cosmic sources.


                                                                                                            Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
In FY 2025, the “Flight Optics Test Evaluation and Characterization Lab ” characterization, calibration, and alignment of optical sensors is
a critical task for any space-flight or aircraft sensor program. Proper characterization/calibration/alignment is the culmination of a monumental
effort (that begins with concept design and runs through fabrication, integration, and environmental testing) that directly impacts the quality of
the science and data products from the sensor. The Flight Optics Test Evaluation and Characterization (FOTEC) facility is essential in supporting
new space-flight hardware for instrumentation for geostationary and/or low Earth orbit mission flights via a NASA or a DoD sponsored program.
This infrastructure will position the NRL to be competitive in both the DoD and civilian government sectors for future programs.

In FY 2026, the “Laboratory for Cognitive Performance Assessment in Immersive Environments” acquisition of a full augmented reality
and biometric sensor suite, including a suite of artificial and virtual reality (AR/VR) headsets, eye trackers, and EEG sensors will enable
researchers to investigate how physiology, perception, and behavior impact usability and adoption. In turn, this will allow NRL to develop
innovative products tailored to the unique needs of the warfighter community, optimizing human strengths and complementing them with user-
informed technologies. All tools will be selected to support portability and cross-division integration with existing equipment, as well as the
ability to be deployed in secure environments, ensuring usefulness across a range of potential use cases and research questions. This asset is
expected to enable NRL to perform state of the art human subjects research by utilizing biometric data to make effective and cognitive inferences
about human performance as users interact with cutting edge AR and VR technologies. These findings will be applied to enhance existing
products and develop bespoke applications in support of the warfighter. The laboratory will integrate with existing systems and technologies
currently being used for research and development across NRL and function as a center for collaboration and data sharing in support of user-
centered design.

Expeditionary Prototyping Facility #2

Prototype Additive Manufacturing (AM) LRP
This project will construct additional space that will allow for one larger collaborative space for the entire Prototype, additive manufacturing,
reverse engineering, and manufacturing technology teams. The constructed space will be a high bay are which will allow for larger sized
equipment and crane support. This project will provide an enhanced prototype environment which will improve workflow and shorten cycle
times by developing a collaborative space for the design and test engineers with the artisans manufacturing and inspecting the parts. The single
shared space will create more efficient workflow paths leading to reduced turnaround time on both engineering developed solutions and urgent
Fleet requirements. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

 PM SSO LUNCHBOX
 This investment expands the Main SCIF in Point Mugu from 2468 SqFt to 4550 SqFt, utilizing space currently occupied by the Scientific and
 Technical Intelligence Liaison Office (STILO) function in an adjacent secure collateral space. The STILO function will be retained in a smaller
 collateral space and within the expanded SCIF. The construction will retrofit all space to meet ICD-705 standards. With increasing demand for
 SCIF facilities to support new and on-going work, current Point Mugu facilities are fully utilized and many times (daily) customers/WD
 workforce are forced to re-schedule or find an alternative work around. Point Mugu has 2 SCIFs (main SCIF in 3008, and a program SCIF in
 3015.) Current demand in PM main SCIF exceeds capacity.

This project is under the LRP Authority of not to exceed $9M.

 project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

 Multi Mission Data Link Lab LRP
 This proposal will construct a new facility to add RDT&E lab space supporting integration and testing for the NAWCAD multi mission data link
 capability. Alternatives have been considered, however this project is the most cost-effective solution for the government.

 LRP #2 ASD CENTRAL OFFICE
 Facility and space that is compliant with ICD 705 with additional RF shielding attenuation at 80db. This additional physical security requirement
 was levied on certain facilities at NBVC Point Mugu. This new footprint facility would be part of the overall POAM created to achieve the new
 requirement.

 Justification: NSWC

 Pre-investment economic analyses were performed for all investments.



                                                                                                              Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
Minor Construction projects replace obsolete facilities, consolidate operations for productivity increases, provide state of the art processing areas
for new research & development missions, and correct environmental/safety deficiencies. Minor construction projects include all costs to deliver
a complete and usable project. Minor Construction is used at the Naval Warfare Centers to: (1) modify existing spaces and construct new
facilities to provide suitable space to design and test new equipment for the surface warfare community; (2) improve security measures and
provide increase security for new initiatives; (3) reduce operating expenses by building or improving government owned facilities so that leased
space, high maintenance space, or portable space may be vacated; (4) reduce energy consumption by installing energy efficient building systems;
(6) modify existing systems to bring facilities up to current building, safety, or environmental codes. Failure to make these investments may
render our infrastructure and facilities unable to support modern technologies and operational capabilities, pose environmental risks, and may
result in human casualties in the event of structural collapse or some other unforeseen catastrophe. Minor Construction projects such as
buildings and warehouses have an estimated useful life of 40 years; minor construction projects such as towers, wharves, and docks have an
estimated useful life of 20 years. The average payback period is 13 years.

Replacement:

PROJECTS ABOVE $1M

FY24 High Power RF Indoor Testing Safety Provisions- $1,430K (NSWC Crane; Crane, IN) - The B-3168 Large Anechoic Chamber
(LAC) contains the Electronic Attack Test and Evaluation System (EATES) test setup. EATES provides a High-Power Radio Frequency (RF)
test and measurement capability for Electronic Attack (EA) and Radar systems. Improvements to the chamber are required to provide the proper
safety posture for a High-Power RF Test Capability asset. The air bladder inflation system of the LAC Sliding Door has failed, and is not
working properly, needing repair/refurbishment. The LAC Sliding Door provides Electromagnetic Interference (EMI) RF shielding protection
when the door is closed. RF Safety is compromised without proper sliding door operation. Also, NSWC Crane Safety has identified that Fire
Safety Protection provisions need to be added to the chamber prior to modifications & improvements that are planned for the future. Propose
performing high power RF risk reduction testing and analysis on proposed safety equipment to assess RF compatibility before pursuing future
High-Power RF mods. The payback period for this investment is 11.5 years.

FY24 Dahlgren Proving Ground Operations Center– $7,900K (NSWC Dahlgren; Dahlgren, VA) - Project renovates the existing structure
of B997 while also adding to the second floor. The first floor will be entirely OSS (possibly SCIF) excluding badge control and consist of
completely reconfigurable Live, Virtual & Constructive (LVC) spaces with a large video wall as well as a viewing area for VIP personnel. The
second floor will add square footage and renovate the area that is already occupied by range control and be entirely Unclassified. The exterior of
the building will be resurfaced, a parking lot and access road will be added, and some exterior mechanical devices will be screened off.
"NSWC transferred $7,900K operating authority to contract authority; a process locally termed a “capital surcharge”, to execute this project in
accordance with Title 10 U.S. Code 2363. It executes as a part of NSWC’s Naval Innovative Science and Engineering (NISE) program. The
payback period for this investment is 14.4 years.

FY25 Re-Conductoring 3-Inch Circuit & East Tie Line - Construction– $1,716K (NSWC Crane; Crane, IN) – New construction will
consist of upgrading approximately 5,000 - Linear Feet (LF) of 3ø, 12.47 kV overhead distribution on the East Tie Line (ETL) circuit and 1,000
LF on the 3 Inch Line (3IL) Circuit. This will include upgrading from the existing copper lines to a combination of #477 ACSR and 2/0 ACSR
QUAIL primary conductors and 4/0 and #2 ACSR neutral conductors. New class 1 wood poles, fiberglass cross arms, fused cut outs, capacitor
banks, pole & pad mounted transformers, and air break switches will also be installed as part of the upgrades. Once reconductoring is complete,
the respective circuit breaker relays in the substations will have their settings adjusted to the new conductor capacity, and the old conductors
poles will be demolished.

Environmental Capability

PROJECTS ABOVE $1M
N/A

Justification: NUWC

Pre-investment economic analyses were performed for all investments.

Minor Construction projects replace obsolete facilities, consolidate operations for productivity increases, provide state of the art processing areas
for new research & development missions, and correct environmental/safety deficiencies. Minor construction projects include all costs to deliver
a complete and usable project. Minor Construction is used at the Naval Warfare Centers to: (1) modify existing spaces and construct new
facilities to provide suitable space to design and test new equipment for the surface warfare community; (2) improve security measures and
provide increase security for new initiatives; (3) reduce operating expenses by building or improving government owned facilities so that leased

                                                                                                                Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
space, high maintenance space, or portable space may be vacated; (4) reduce energy consumption by installing energy efficient building systems;
(6) modify existing systems to bring facilities up to current building, safety, or environmental codes. Failure to make these investments may
render our infrastructure and facilities unable to support modern technologies and operational capabilities, pose environmental risks, and may
result in human casualties in the event of structural collapse or some other unforeseen catastrophe. Minor Construction projects such as
buildings and warehouses have an estimated useful life of 40 years; minor construction projects such as towers, wharves, and docks have an
estimated useful life of 20 years. The average payback period is 13 years.

cleaning areas will be improved, and the component curing oven size will be increased. Construction will include the remove all non-bearing

REPLACEMENT

PROJECTS UNDER $1M:

The investment provides a design to create a space with high powered requirements for advanced machinery to create new Warfighter systems
through On-Demand Manufacturing (ODM). An economic analysis will be performed as part of the planning process. Without this investment,
there will not be a dedicated area to support the high-power requirements to support current ODM equipment. This project is part of the LRDP.
The investment provides a design to convert a space to an Open Secret Storage (OSS0 space. An economic analysis will be performed as part of
the planning process. Without this investment, there will be insufficient space to conduct distribution of capabilities. This project is part of the
LRP. This is a Naval Innovative Science and Engineering (NISE) project.

PROJECTS ABOVE $1M:

The "Cybersecurity Development Laboratory Modernization” replacement project in FY24 will provide a secure laboratory space. An
economic analysis and independent government estimate (IGE) will be performed as part of the planning process. Without this investment,
sponsor engineering and development requirements will not be met, negatively impacting secure Warfighter communications. This is a NISE
project.

The “Keys and Codes Engineering Laboratory Modernization” replacement project in FY25 will upgrade a current the laboratory to a secure
space housing key management system engineering and development. This project will fill a critical cyber laboratory deficit. An economic
analysis will be performed as part of the planning process, once the scope has been finalized. An independent government estimate (IGE) has
been validated by NAVFAC. Without this investment, there will be in inability to maintain critical key management systems, negatively
impacting the warfighter secure communications. This is a NISE project.




                                                                                                                Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
The "Building 198 Manufacturing Innovation Area” construction project in FY25 will create the facility where the NIWC team will be able
to able to develop new systems to better support our warfighter through On-Demand Manufacturing (ODM) methodologies in a safe and secure
environment. The design for the Manufacturing Innovation Area will include laboratory area for 3D scanning of existing systems and
workbenches for 3D modeling and digital twin coordination. Additionally, the design will also include laboratory space for automated machine
tools such as laser-cutters, subtractive manufacturing machines, and 3-D printers to permit rapid prototyping and hybrid production of new
systems. The design will include space with high power requirements for advanced machinery, flexible and modular electrical busways,
additional mechanical filtration, exhaust systems, and industrial grade finishes and components. Without this investment, there will not be a
dedicated area with the proper high-power requirements that are needed to support the proper function of current ODM equipment. This project
is part of the LRP. This is a NISE project.

The "Building 180 Saint Julien's Creek Reconfiguration” replacement project in FY25 will renovate the space converting it to an Open Secret
Storage (OSS) Space. The project will undergo installation of new walls, offices, lighting upgrades, ceiling replacement, new roof, new gutters,
upgraded fire protection system, electrical upgrades, mechanical upgrades, restroom renovations, and handicap accessibility throughout the
facility. An economic analysis will be completed. Without this investment, the Command will have inefficient space to distribute innovative
capabilities. This project is part of the LRP. This is a NISE project.

The “Model Range Arch" project in FY25 replaces the Model Range Antenna Pattern Range (APR), a unique test facility for scale brass High
Frequency and full-scale High Frequency/Very High Frequency/Ultra High Frequency (HF and full-scale Hf/VDF/UHF) antenna measurements,
that has been in continual use for 25 years and shows signs of structural instability. Project will support Brass and Numerical Modeling Studies
(BNMS) and Electromagnetic Resonators for Signal Intelligence (ELFIN). If the investment is not funded, the Navy will lose High Frequency
(HF) scale brass model analysis capability, a major impact to shipboard HF broadband and Direction Finding (DF) array antenna performance.
The authority requested in FY 2025 for Minor Construction (Replacement) is planning and solicitation development costs for a project that will
occur in FY 2026.

The” Building 180 Saint Julien's Creek Reconfiguration Construction” project in FY25 will allow the entire building to undergo a conversion
from unclassified space to an Open Secret Storage (OSS) Space, per DoDM 5200.01. This renovation project will address existing structural
components that currently do not meet minimum physical security requirements set by the Unified Facilities Criteria (UFC) and National
Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST) criteria. This building currently operates as administrative space; however, the new interior layout
design will convert some of the space to a dual lab with open bay areas consisting of lab workshops, material storage areas, and offices. The
scope of work includes installation of new walls, adding enclosed offices, lighting upgrades, ceiling replacement, a new roof, gutters, upgrades to
the fire protection system, painted surfaces, and handicap accessibility throughout the building. This project upgrades the building's interior
spaces to include electrical, mechanical, plumbing, Information Technology (IT) infrastructure, renovation of restrooms, and communication
systems. This project will meet the needs of the Command’s requirement to increase the amount of OSS space needed for various command
Integrated Product Teams (IPTs). If this project is not executed, then Naval Information Warfare Center (NIWC) Atlantic (LANT) will not have

                                                                                                               Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
sufficient space to distribute increased innovative capabilities to the Naval workforce. The economic analysis will be developed as part of the
DD1391 package. This project is part of the Laboratory Revitalization Demonstration Program (LRDP). This is a NISE project.

The “B3113 Lab 6 Renovation Construction project in FY26 will include design and construction of the 8,000 SF facility to be demolished to
internal studs and rebuilt. Spaces to be updated within the existing boundary with new finishes. The building renovation will include demolishing
select existing MEP system within the boundaries that include furniture, electrical lines, lighting, and exhaust system. New construction will
include limited wall construction, undated machinal, electrical and finishes. The current administrative configuration will be converted to a dual
lab and administrative working layout. The proposed future occupants could include the Electronic Security System (ESS) teams of Command
& Control, Intelligence, Surveillance, & Reconnaissance (C2ISR) with associated competency supervisors. The users currently in space will be
relocated as part of this project. A full FF&E package with NIWC standard workstations and select equipment will be included with the design
and reconfiguration of the interior space. Building systems will be properly sized and upgraded to all current standards and codes for
mechanical, electrical, communication, and fire protection. Building will be ABA compliant. If not renovated, NIWC will still have a need for
additional lab space. This project is part the Laboratory Revitalization Demonstration Program (LRDP). - This is a NISE project

PROJECTS ABOVE $1M:

The “Automated Digital Network System (ADNS) Laboratory" project in FY24 provides laboratory spaces to deliver critical capabilities to
the warfighter and to meet mission requirements and to serve as the tactical Wide Area Network (WAN) for Navy Internet Protocol (IP) network
operations for ship-to-ship and ship-to-shore communications. ADNS is a critical system for the afloat, air, subsurface and ashore warfighters
and delivers critical capabilities, products and services to the fleet. An economic analysis has been performed as part of the proposal
process. A formal net present value life-cycle economic analysis has been completed as part of the DD Form 1391 approval process as required



                                                                                                              Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
in OPNAVINST 11010.20H. If the investment is not funded, it will impact the ability to meet sponsor requirements and rapidly deliver current
and next generation capabilities, products and services to the fleet. This is a Laboratory Revitalization Program (LRP) project.

The "Swimmer Interdiction Security System (SISS) Bangor Topside Facilities" project in FY24 provides prefabricated structures, in place
of 11-year-old trailers, to enhance Marine Mammal Program (MMP) in support of mission requirements for hardware, personnel, veterinary, and
boat response. An economic analysis will be performed as part of the internal proposal process. If the investment is not funded, the aged trailers
will continue to be utilized minimal available space and decreasing efficient workflows.

The “Sixth Street Modular Complex” project in FY24 includes site work to establish foundations and utilities infrastructure for four to eight
modular buildings, roughly 48’ x 100’ each. There is an increasing demand of secure space within the command. Modular construction is faster
and less expensive compared to new construction and hardening existing spaces. Future buildings will be customizable and funded as needed
based on individual project requirements. This is a NISE project.

The “Outdoor Laser Test Range” construction project in FY 24 consists of two laser test ranges. One range is a 2.0 KM (1.25 miles) located
within a forested area. The other range is 1.2 KM (0.75 miles) across open water. Both ranges are located to minimize interference with other
land uses. The ranges will be used to test and develop laser equipment for free space optics and communications. - This is a NISE project. The
"Tactical Computer Networks Environment (TCNE) Laboratory Expansion" project in FY25 increases laboratory space to support Tactical
Networks Division's expanding requirement to develop, integrate, and certify network systems for the Fleet. A detailed cost analysis will be
performed as part of the planning process once the scope has been finalized, and independent government estimate (IGE) has been completed. If
the investment is not funded, it will impact the ability to deliver Information Warfare Dominance through secure and reliable networks. This is a
Laboratory Revitalization Program (LRP) project. The “New Lab St Julien’s Creek” Construction project in FY26 will construct a new
structure to support new secure spaces. These secure spaces will include administration, lab, and S-VCT Conference room capability. This is
roughly 10,000 SF facility to be designed with a flexible design while using durable material. The security requirements will vary with different
levels. New construction will include (except for the vestibule area) separation of lab space with server capability, offices, breakroom, restrooms,

The “Command, Control, Communication, Computers, Cyber Defense and Combat Systems and Intelligence, Surveillance and
Reconnaissance (C6ISR) Test and Evaluation Platform” project in FY24 will expand and replace the existing outdoor operations testing area
and provide a properly configured staging and testing area within a fenced outdoor compound. It will include construction of a concrete pad for

                                                                                                               Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
staging requirements, underground power service, and installation of external power, and security fencing. The compound will include a 9,900
square feet Rubb building with shipping/receiving, assembly, storage rack, workbench areas, outdoor equipment staging areas, and correctly
positioned concrete antenna pads. The new compound and Rubb building will provide the lab space required to build, test, and evaluate C6ISR
system operations. It will also provide space to store back-up antennas and related equipment. The Test and Evaluation Platform will provide
adequate electronics test and integration space needed to support equipment development, programming, testing, rack integration, and
deployable equipment construction by the C6ISR Integrated Project Team (IPT). Once the outdoor compound and the Rubb building is
complete, the existing staging area will be demolished. An economic analysis has been performed. Without this investment, the C6ISR system
operations will be limited, and the area will be insufficient to house highly sensitive deployable equipment. This project is part of the LRP. This
is a NISE project.

emerging technologies in UASs and Robotics. Current projects such as Advanced Communication Systems (ACS) within mobile wireless

integration efforts. No facility currently provides indoor Research Development Test and Evaluation (RDT&E) space to support vehicle On-The-
Move systems demonstration and integration, UAVs/UASs/Robotics operations or any large systems testing in a controlled environment. An
economic analysis will be performed as part of the planning process. Without this investment, there will be no facility that can support controlled
environment testing of large systems UAV’s/UAS’s. This project is part of the LRP. This is a NISE project.

with the design and reconfiguration of the interior space. Building systems will be properly sized to all current standards and codes for
mechanical, electrical, water, sewer, communication, and fire protection. Building will be ABA compliant. The existing roof covering, gutters,
and roof protrusions need to be evaluated for restoration and/or replaced as required. If unapproved, NIWC will be unable to relocate teams out
of current facilities, that require full renovation for OSS and secure spaces. This project is part of the Laboratory Revitalization Demonstration
Program (LRDP). This is a NISE project.

Justification: NRL

PROJECTS OVER $1M
The project over $1M in FY 2024 are the “Backup Generator Bldg A47”. The “Backup Generator Bldg A47” the project will provide a 1500
KVA emergency backup generator to provide emergency power as well as a secondary unit substation, primary and secondary metering, main
building switchgear, exhaust fan and air handling units. The upgrades will allow the Chilled Water Plant to supply chilled water to conditioned
spaces among eighteen buildings throughout the NRL campus during an electrical outage.



                                                                                                              Exhibit Fund-9B Capital Investment Justification
The project over $1M in FY 2025 is the “Install Generator to support Chemistry Division”. The “Install Generator to support Chemistry
Division” project currently is running with only a temporary backup system - if there is a power outage, Research & Development Services
Division contracts for a generator to be procured and situated on a trailer parked behind the building to supply temporary power. The Chemistry
division has more than 100 laboratories, each with their own specialized equipment, so an outage could jeopardize several ongoing research
programs. Equipment associated with these such as refrigerators, freezers, glove boxes, and fume hoods are essential to their mission and we
estimate that an outage costs approximately $225,000 per event. Without the addition of this CIP project, there will be intermittent loss of
functionality whenever the power is lost. In the event of an emergency where power is lost, research potential is reduced when chemistry
samples require controlled low temperature environments or when fume hoods and glove boxes lose pressure.

The project over $1M in FY 2026 is the “Cyber Laboratory Addition”. The “Cyber Laboratory Addition” project provides command,
control, communications, network engineering, and management of new and on-orbit assets, including both operational and experimental
spacecraft. Construction of a Blossom Point Cyber Lab would enhance in-house cyber security capabilities, reducing the need for expensive
third-party services, and mitigating detrimental security breaches. The Cyber Lab will foster innovation and skills development, proprietary
software development, and training programs leading to more efficient threat detection and response, ultimately furthering the NRL research and
development initiatives. Additionally, by positioning itself as a leader in cybersecurity research, the Cyber Lab could attract investment, grants,
and contracts, further fueling its expansion and long-term sustainability.

Justification: EXWC

In FY2026, EXWC is requesting Naval Innovative Science and Engineering (NISE) Capital Investment project to revitalize and modernize the
Oceans Waterfront Laboratory Facility PH1393. The NAVFAC EXWC Oceans Waterfront laboratory, located at Naval Base Ventura County,
Port Hueneme, provides vital research and development, test and evaluation and fabrication capabilities to the Navy and DoD. The Waterfront
Laboratory requires revitalization/ modernization to support emergent and future RDT&E efforts to provide support capability for multiple users
and projects in direct support of undersea warfare for the Navy and the DoD.

The revitalization/ modernization will formally repurpose the facility to provide future mission support as a lab space for fabrication,
prototyping, maintenance and repair of mission systems and support equipment. The facility was constructed in the early 1980’s to support the
wash-down and cleaning of the solid rocket boosters associated with the NASA space program and has not had repairs or modifications since
original construction. The revitalization/ modernization effort will repair and reconfigure bays A and B, repair and upgrade the building
electrical system, and telecom system. This work is all required to support increased capability and capacity while meeting current building and
ADA codes.

4. Transportation

                                NARRATIVE
                        DEPARTMENT OF THE NAVY
              TRANSPORTATION – MILITARY SEALIFT COMMAND
                 FISCAL YEAR (FY) 2026 PRESIDENT’S BUDGET
                                  JUNE 2025

Mission Statement / Overview:
The Military Sealift Command (MSC) comprises the NWCF’s transportation business and
is the single manager‐operating agency for sealift services. The primary focus of MSC
includes over‐ocean movement of supplies and provisions to the deployed operating
forces and maintaining prepositioned equipment and supplies. These services combine to
support the Department of the Navy (DON) in deterring potential threats and promptly
responding to crises in the maritime crossroads. MSC provides support to Naval Fleet
Commanders and Department of Defense (DoD) activities by providing unique vessels
and programs. MSC evaluates mission performance by measuring readiness of ships and
crews as well as interoperability with the Fleet and joint forces.

FY 2026 budget includes Risk reduction initiatives to facilitate the achievement of Civilian
Mariner manning standards, improve operational readiness and generate a Force ready
to fight in a future contested logistics environment. Aligned with SECDEF priorities for
mission readiness, approximately $1.4 billion was realigned from Navy Working Capital
Fund to OMN in FY 2026 to support maintenance and repair requirements for Military
Sealift Command, allowing the Department to address maintenance shortfalls, risk based
and holistically across the entire Fleet.

Activity Group Composition:
MSC supports the United States Pacific Fleet, the U.S. Fleet Forces Command, the Naval
Sea Systems Command, the Naval Information Warfare Systems Command, the Strategic
Systems Programs, the Naval Special Warfare Command, Missile Defense Agency, the
U.S. Air Force, and various other customers with unique vessels.

The four programs budgeted through the Navy Working Capital Fund (NWCF) are:

Combat Logistics Force (CLF): Provides support utilizing civilian mariner manned non‐
combatant ships for material support including underway replenishment, commercial
helicopter services and other direct fleet support to Navy ships worldwide.

Special Mission Ships (SMS): Provides unique seagoing platforms, which support
specialized scientific and technical missions for DoD sponsors. Missions include ocean
surveillance, oceanographic survey, cable laying, missile telemetry collection, submarine
support and navigation test support.

Afloat Prepositioning Force‐Navy (APF‐N): Deploys advance material for strategic lifts
and at‐sea staging around the world for the U.S. Navy and Marine Expeditionary Forces.
This program also contains the Expeditionary Transfer Dock (ESD) and Expeditionary Sea
Base (ESB) ship classes, which are highly flexible platforms, utilized across a broad range

                        DEPARTMENT OF THE NAVY
              TRANSPORTATION – MILITARY SEALIFT COMMAND
                 FISCAL YEAR (FY) 2026 PRESIDENT’S BUDGET
                                  JUNE 2025

of military operations supporting the deployment and sustainment of forces and
prepositioned supplies and equipment.

Service Support Ships (SSS): Provides the Navy with towing, rescue and salvage,
submarine support, floating medical facilities, as well as the Navy’s 6th Fleet Flagship.
Also included are Expeditionary Fast Transports (EPF), which provide rapid, intra‐theater
transport of conventional, or Special Forces and military equipment and supplies. Support
ships include Fleet Ocean Tugs, Rescue and Salvage Ships, Hospital Ships, Submarine

Tenders, Command Ship, High Speed Transport Vessels, the contracted Harbor Tugs and
Tows, and Motor Vessels (MVs).

Significant Changes since the FY2025 President’s Budget:

CLF – The CLF summary details a significant restructuring of fleet operations,
deactivations, activations, and budgetary allocations in anticipation of increasing
operational readiness in FY 2026. Changes including activation of USNS Lucy Stone and
USNS Sojourner Truth and inactivation of USNS Pecos and USNS John Ericsson
scheduled in FY 2026. Similarly, FY 2026 provides increased Pacific Fleet chartered
vessels to support additional coastal tankers, accelerated research, development, and
fielding of an At‐Sea Rearm Vertical Launch System (VLS) (ASRV) capability for the
Expeditionary Transfer Dock (ESD) vessels. In support of Maintenance and Repair
(M&R) transition from Navy Working Capital Fund (NWCF) to Operations and
Maintenance, Navy (OMN) appropriation, $969.32 millions were realigned out of NWCF
reimbursable authority in FY 2026.

SMS‐ The increase in SMS portfolio is due to sustainment of Auxiliary General Ocean
Surveillance (T‐AGOS), Auxiliary General Survey (T‐AGS), Auxiliary General Survey
Vessel, Contract Operated (T‐AGSE). The USNS Waters was funded for engineering
upgrades in FY 2026. The USNS Zeus was retired and will be replaced with a long‐term
chartered vessel for undersea cable operations until the Auxiliary Cable Repair Ship (T‐
ARC(X)) replacement vessel is delivered. In support of M&R transition from NWCF to
OMN, $95.82 millions were realigned out of NWCF reimbursable authority in FY 2026.

APF‐N – The Maritime Prepositioning Force (MPF) was increased for operations and
maintenance support in FY 2026. Increase includes extension in operation of USNS John
Glenn before inactivation. APF‐N funds were also transferred to support the accelerated
research, development, and fielding of an At‐Sea Rearm Vertical Launch System (VLS)
(ASRV) capability for the Expeditionary Transfer Dock (ESD) vessels. In support of

MSC operates under four distinct unit cost goals ‐ one for each of its programs. All
programs have cost/per day as the unit cost basis (costs include only per Diem expenses
in the Annual Operating Budget (AOB). Ship inventory levels by ship class and ship
availability status including FOS, ROS, deployment or undergoing shipyard Maintenance
and Repair impacts unit cost levels. Costs in all years are primarily a function of approved
escalation, fuel, Civilian Mariner salaries, and Maintenance and Repair.

NOTE: Change CY, BY1, and BY2 to the fiscal years for the budget submission. For Example CY = FY 2020; BY1 = FY 2021; BY2 = FY 2022

Narrative Justification: This exhibit will provide detailed justification by line item in support of summary capital investment purchases shown on the Fund‐9a Exhibit.
    ‐     Describe the enhancement afforded by the existing equipment/ADPE and telecommunications resources/software development/facility and the shortcomings inherent in the
          current situation.
    ‐     Describe the benefits to be realized from the proposed capital investment.
    ‐     Indicate whether an economic analysis or cost analysis has been performed and, if not, why not. Summarize the net present value advantages of the proposed investment
          over alternatives considered and discarded. Be prepared to provide a copy of supporting economic analysis upon request.
    ‐     For MILCON projects, provide a copy of the supporting Form 1391 for new projects not previously submitted or identified.
    ‐     Describe the impact of not making the proposed capital investment.
    ‐     For computer software, separately identify license fees.
               ‐     Alternatively, dollars in millions may be used out to three decimal places
Column Entries
    A. Element of Cost. For items purchased under the Project/Line Item, provide applicable subcategories (e.g. vehicles may be broken down into cars, trucks, buses, etc.). For
          Software provide the item, and if applicable, break into module delivery subcategories.
    B. Quantity. Provide the approximate number of items to be purchased under the subcategory or as applicable for software.
    C. Per Unit Cost. Enter the actual or estimated unit cost, when appropriate, for each element listed. Express unit costs in thousands of dollars, to the nearest tenth (i.e., $20.1
          thousand). Unit costs should be expressed in terms of “then year” costs.
    D. Guidance on Unspecified Minor Construction Thresholds

10 U.S. Code § 2805 ‐ Unspecified minor construction
   (a) Authority to Carry Out Unspecified Minor Military Construction Projects.— (1)Within an amount equal to 125 percent of the amount authorized by law for such purpose, the
   Secretary concerned may carry out unspecified minor military construction projects not otherwise authorized by law.
   (2)An unspecified minor military construction project is a military construction project that has an approved cost equal to or less than $3,000,000. However, if the military
   construction project is intended solely to correct a deficiency that is life‐threatening, health‐threatening, or safety‐threatening, an unspecified minor
   military construction project may have an approved cost equal to or less than $4,000,000.
   (d) Laboratory Revitalization.— (1)For the revitalization and recapitalization of laboratories owned by the United States and under the jurisdiction of the Secretary concerned, the
   Secretary concerned may obligate and expend— (A)from appropriations available to the Secretary concerned for operation and maintenance, amounts necessary to carry out an
   unspecified minor military construction project costing not more than $4,000,000, notwithstanding subsection (c); or
   (B)from appropriations available to the Secretary concerned for military construction not otherwise authorized by law or from funds authorized to be made available under section
   219(a) of the Duncan Hunter National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2009 (Public Law 110–417; 10 U.S.C. 2358 note), amounts necessary to carry out an unspecified
   minor military construction project costing not more than $4,000,000.
  (2)For purposes of this subsection, an unspecified minor military construction project is a military construction project that (notwithstanding subsection (a)) has an approved cost
  equal to or less than $4,000,000. The Secretary of Defense shall establish procedures for the review and approval of requests from the Secretary of a military department to carry
  out a construction project under this subsection.
  (3)Not later than February 1, 2014, the Secretary of Defense shall submit to the congressional defense committees a report on the use of the authority provided by this subsection.
  The report shall include a list and description of the construction projects carried out under this subsection, including the location and cost of each project.
  (4)In this subsection, the term “laboratory” includes— (A)a research, engineering, and development center; and

  (B)a test and evaluation activity.
  (5)The authority to carry out a project under this subsection expires on September 30, 2018.
